1.5x,
http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/The_Beatles_in_America.JPG/440px-The_Beatles_in_America.JPG
2x"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:The_Beatles_in_America.JPG"
target="_blank"
class="internal"
title="Enlarge"><img
src="http://sp.ask.com/sh/i/wiki/magnify-clip.png"
width="15"
height="11"
alt=""
/></a>










</div>
Harrison
(third
from
left)
with
the
other
Beatles
in
New
York
City
in
1964









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>By
1965's
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rubber_Soul?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rubber
Soul">Rubber
Soul</a></i>,
Harrison
had
begun
to
lead
the
other
Beatles
into
<a
href="/wiki/Folk_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Folk
rock">folk
rock</a>
through
his
interest
in
the
Byrds
and
Bob
Dylan,
and
towards
Indian
classical
music
through
his
use
of
the
sitar
on
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Norwegian_Wood_(This_Bird_Has_Flown)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Norwegian
Wood
(This
Bird
Has
Flown)">Norwegian
Wood
(This
Bird
Has
Flown)</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-30"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-32"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>nb
2<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
later
called
<i>Rubber
Soul</i>
his
&quot;favourite
[Beatles]
album&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_Beatles2000194_33-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_Beatles2000194-33"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i><a
href="/wiki/Revolver_(Beatles_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Revolver
(Beatles
album)">Revolver</a></i>
(1966)
included
three
of
his
compositions:
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Taxman?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Taxman">Taxman</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Love_You_To?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Love
You
To">Love
You
To</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Want_to_Tell_You?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Want
to
Tell
You">I
Want
to
Tell
You</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-34"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup>
His
introduction
of
the
drone-like
<a
href="/wiki/Tanpura_(instrument)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tanpura
(instrument)">tambura</a>
part
on
Lennon's
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Tomorrow_Never_Knows?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tomorrow
Never
Knows">Tomorrow
Never
Knows</a>&quot;
exemplified
the
band's
ongoing
exploration
of
non-Western
instruments.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett199935.E2.80.9336_35-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett199935.E2.80.9336-35"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
<a
href="/wiki/Tabla?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tabla">tabla</a>-driven
&quot;Love
You
To&quot;
was
the
Beatles'
first
genuine
foray
into
Indian
music.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett199940.E2.80.9342_36-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett199940.E2.80.9342-36"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup>
According
to
the
<a
href="/wiki/Ethnomusicology?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ethnomusicology">ethnomusicologist</a>
David
Reck,
the
song
set
a
precedent
in
popular
music
as
an
example
of
Asian
culture
being
represented
by
Westerners
respectfully
and
without
parody.<sup
id="cite_ref-37"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
Harrison
continued
to
develop
his
interest
in
non-Western
instrumentation,
playing
<a
href="/wiki/Swarmandal?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Swarmandal">swarmandal</a>
on
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Strawberry_Fields_Forever?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Strawberry
Fields
Forever">Strawberry
Fields
Forever</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinn200974_38-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinn200974-38"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>By
late
1966
Harrison's
interests
had
moved
away
from
the
Beatles,
as
reflected
in
his
choice
of
Eastern
<a
href="/wiki/Guru?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Guru">gurus</a>
and
religious
leaders
for
inclusion
on
the
album
cover
for
<i><a
href="/wiki/Sgt._Pepper%27s_Lonely_Hearts_Club_Band?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sgt.
Pepper's
Lonely
Hearts
Club
Band">Sgt.
Pepper's
Lonely
Hearts
Club
Band</a></i>
in
1967.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETillery201159.E2.80.9360_39-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETillery201159.E2.80.9360-39"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-41"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>nb
3<span>]</span></a></sup>
His
sole
composition
on
the
album
was
the
Indian-inspired
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Within_You_Without_You?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Within
You
Without
You">Within
You
Without
You</a>&quot;,
to
which
no
other
Beatle
contributed.<sup
id="cite_ref-42"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
played
sitar
and
tambura
on
the
track,
backed
by
musicians
from
the
London
<a
href="/wiki/Asian_Music_Circle?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Asian
Music
Circle">Asian
Music
Circle</a>
on
<a
href="/wiki/Esraj?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Esraj">dilruba</a>,
swarmandal
and
tabla.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006178.E2.80.93179_43-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006178.E2.80.93179-43"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-45"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>nb
4<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1968
his
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_Inner_Light_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Inner
Light
(song)">The
Inner
Light</a>&quot;
was
recorded
at
the
EMI
Studios
in
<a
href="/wiki/Mumbai?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mumbai">Bombay</a>,
featuring
a
group
of
local
musicians
playing
traditional
Indian
instruments.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETillery201163_46-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETillery201163-46"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup>
Released
as
the
B-side
to
McCartney's
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Lady_Madonna?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lady
Madonna">Lady
Madonna</a>&quot;,
it
was
the
first
Harrison
composition
to
appear
on
a
Beatles
single.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETillery201163_46-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETillery201163-46"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup>
Derived
from
a
quotation
from
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Tao_Te_Ching?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tao
Te
Ching">Tao
Te
Ching</a></i>,
the
song's
lyric
reflected
Harrison's
deepening
interest
in
Hinduism
and
<a
href="/wiki/Transcendental_Meditation?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Transcendental
Meditation">meditation</a>,
while
musically
it
embraced
the
<a
href="/wiki/Carnatic_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Carnatic
music">Karnatak</a>
discipline
of
Indian
music,
rather
than
the
<a
href="/wiki/Hindustani_classical_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hindustani
classical
music">Hindustani</a>
style
of
his
previous
work
in
the
genre.<sup
id="cite_ref-47"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Dylan
and
<a
href="/wiki/The_Band?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Band">the
Band</a>
were
a
major
musical
influence
on
Harrison
at
the
end
of
his
career
with
the
Beatles.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng200652_48-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng200652-48"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
established
a
friendship
with
Dylan
and
found
himself
drawn
to
the
Band's
sense
of
communal
music-making
and
to
the
creative
equality
among
the
band
members,
in
contrast
with
Lennon
and
McCartney's
domination
of
the
Beatles'
songwriting
and
creative
direction.
This
coincided
with
a
prolific
period
in
his
songwriting
and
his
growing
desire
to
assert
his
independence
from
the
band.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng200639.E2.80.9352_49-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng200639.E2.80.9352-49"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup>
During
the
recording
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Beatles_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Beatles
(album)">The
Beatles</a></i>
in
1968,
tensions
ran
high,
and
drummer
<a
href="/wiki/Ringo_Starr?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ringo
Starr">Ringo
Starr</a>
quit
briefly.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992295.E2.80.93296_50-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992295.E2.80.93296-50"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup>
Harrison's
songwriting
contributions
to
the
album
included
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/While_My_Guitar_Gently_Weeps?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="While
My
Guitar
Gently
Weeps">While
My
Guitar
Gently
Weeps</a>&quot;,
which
featured
<a
href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Eric
Clapton">Eric
Clapton</a>
on
lead
guitar,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Piggies?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Piggies">Piggies</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Long,_Long,_Long?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Long,
Long,
Long">Long,
Long,
Long</a>&quot;,
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Savoy_Truffle?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Savoy
Truffle">Savoy
Truffle</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-51"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup>
Tensions
among
the
Beatles
surfaced
again
during
the
filming
of
rehearsals
at
<a
href="/wiki/Twickenham_Film_Studios?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Twickenham
Film
Studios">Twickenham
Studios</a>
in
January
1969
for
what
became
the
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Let_It_Be?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Let
It
Be">Let
It
Be</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng200639.E2.80.9352_49-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng200639.E2.80.9352-49"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup>
Frustrated
by
the
poor
working
conditions
in
the
cold
and
sterile
film
studio,
as
well
as
by
what
he
perceived
as
Lennon's
creative
disengagement
from
the
Beatles
and
a
domineering
attitude
from
McCartney,
Harrison
quit
the
group
on
10
January,
but
agreed
to
return
twelve
days
later.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoggett200960.E2.80.9363_52-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoggett200960.E2.80.9363-52"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Relations
among
the
Beatles
were
more
cordial,
though
still
strained,
during
sessions
for
their
final
recorded
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Abbey_Road?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Abbey
Road">Abbey
Road</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles2001354_53-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles2001354-53"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
LP
included
two
of
Harrison's
most
respected
Beatles
compositions:
&quot;Here
Comes
the
Sun&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Something?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Something">Something</a>&quot;,
which
became
one
half
of
the
Beatles'
first
<a
href="/wiki/A-side_and_B-side?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="A-side
and
B-side">double-sided</a>
number
one
single,
Harrison's
first
A-side,
and
his
first
chart
topper.<sup
id="cite_ref-54"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1969
<a
href="/wiki/Frank_Sinatra?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Frank
Sinatra">Frank
Sinatra</a>
recorded
&quot;Something&quot;,
and
later
dubbed
it
&quot;the
greatest
love
song
of
the
past
fifty
years&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFricke2002178_55-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFricke2002178-55"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup>
Lennon
considered
it
the
best
song
on
<i>Abbey
Road</i>,
and
it
became
the
Beatles'
second
most
covered
song
after
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Yesterday?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Yesterday">Yesterday</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-56"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup>
Author
Peter
Lavezzoli
wrote:
&quot;Harrison
would
finally
achieve
equal
songwriting
status&nbsp;…
with
his
two
classic
contributions
to
the
final
Beatles'
LP&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006185_57-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006185-57"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
April
1970
when
Harrison's
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/For_You_Blue?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="For
You
Blue">For
You
Blue</a>&quot;
was
released
in
America
as
a
double
A-side
with
McCartney's
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_Long_and_Winding_Road?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Long
and
Winding
Road">The
Long
and
Winding
Road</a>&quot;,
it
became
the
band's
second
chart-topping
double
A-side
and
&quot;For
You
Blue&quot;
became
Harrison's
second
number
one
hit.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBronson1992275_58-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBronson1992275-58"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup>
His
increased
productivity
and
the
Beatles'
reluctance
to
include
his
songs
on
their
albums
meant
that
by
the
time
of
<a
href="/wiki/Break-up_of_the_Beatles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Break-up
of
the
Beatles">their
break-up</a>
he
had
amassed
a
stockpile
of
unreleased
compositions.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoward200436.E2.80.9337_59-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoward200436.E2.80.9337-59"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup>
While
Harrison
grew
as
a
songwriter,
his
compositional
presence
on
Beatles
albums
remained
limited
to
two
or
three
songs,
increasing
his
frustration,
and
significantly
contributing
to
the
band's
<a
href="/wiki/Break-up_of_the_Beatles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Break-up
of
the
Beatles">break-up</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGeorge-Warren2001413_60-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGeorge-Warren2001413-60"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup>
Harrison's
last
recording
session
with
the
Beatles
was
on
4
January
1970,
when
he,
McCartney
and
Starr
recorded
the
Harrison
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Me_Mine?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Me
Mine">I
Me
Mine</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1988195_61-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1988195-61"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="1968.E2.80.9387:_solo_career">1968–87:
solo
career</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=George_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3"
title="Edit
section:
1968–87:
solo
career">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Early_solo_work">Early
solo
work</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=George_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4"
title="Edit
section:
Early
solo
work">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Before
the
Beatles'
break-up
Harrison
had
already
recorded
and
released
two
solo
albums:
<i><a
href="/wiki/Wonderwall_Music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wonderwall
Music">Wonderwall
Music</a></i>
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/Electronic_Sound?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Electronic
Sound">Electronic
Sound</a></i>,
both
of
which
include
mainly
instrumental
compositions.
<i>Wonderwall
Music</i>,
a
soundtrack
to
the
1968
film
<i><a
href="/wiki/Wonderwall_(film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wonderwall
(film)">Wonderwall</a></i>,
blends
Indian
and
Western
instrumentation,
while
<i>Electronic
Sound</i>
is
an
experimental
album
that
prominently
features
a
<a
href="/wiki/Moog_synthesizer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Moog
synthesizer">Moog
synthesizer</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-62"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup>
Released
in
November
1968,
<i>Wonderwall
Music</i>
was
the
first
solo
album
by
a
Beatle
and
the
first
LP
released
by
<a
href="/wiki/Apple_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Apple
Records">Apple
Records</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-63"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup>
Indian
musicians
<a
href="/wiki/Aashish_Khan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Aashish
Khan">Aashish
Khan</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Shivkumar_Sharma?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Shivkumar
Sharma">Shivkumar
Sharma</a>
performed
on
the
album,
which
contains
the
experimental
<a
href="/wiki/Sound_collage?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sound
collage">sound
collage</a>
&quot;Dream
Scene&quot;,
recorded
several
months
before
Lennon's
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Revolution_9?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Revolution
9">Revolution
9</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-64"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
December
1969
Harrison
participated
in
a
brief
tour
of
Europe
with
the
American
group
<a
href="/wiki/Delaney_%26_Bonnie?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Delaney
&amp;
Bonnie">Delaney
&amp;
Bonnie
and
Friends</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng200663.E2.80.9365_65-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng200663.E2.80.9365-65"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup>
During
the
tour
that
included
Clapton,
<a
href="/wiki/Bobby_Whitlock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bobby
Whitlock">Bobby
Whitlock</a>,
drummer
<a
href="/wiki/Jim_Gordon_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jim
Gordon
(musician)">Jim
Gordon</a>
and
band
leaders
<a
href="/wiki/Delaney_Bramlett?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Delaney
Bramlett">Delaney</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Bonnie_Bramlett?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bonnie
Bramlett">Bonnie
Bramlett</a>,
Harrison
began
to
write
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/My_Sweet_Lord?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="My
Sweet
Lord">My
Sweet
Lord</a>&quot;,
which
became
his
first
single
as
a
solo
artist.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng200667_66-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng200667-66"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup>
Delaney
Bramlett
inspired
Harrison
to
learn
slide
guitar,
significantly
influencing
his
later
music.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng200664.2C_84_67-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng200664.2C_84-67"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="All_Things_Must_Pass"><i>All
Things
Must
Pass</i></span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=George_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5"
title="Edit
section:
All
Things
Must
Pass">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="rellink
relarticle
mainarticle">








Main
article:









<a
href="/wiki/All_Things_Must_Pass?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="All
Things
Must
Pass">All
Things
Must
Pass</a>







</div>








<p>After
years
of
being
restricted
in
his
songwriting
contributions
to
the
Beatles'
albums,
Harrison
released
<i>All
Things
Must
Pass</i>.
It
was
a
<a
href="/wiki/Double_album?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Double
album">triple
album</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchaffner1980155_68-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchaffner1980155-68"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup>
with
two
discs
of
his
songs
and
the
third
of
recordings
of
Harrison
<a
href="/wiki/Jam_session?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jam
session">jamming</a>
with
friends.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoward200436.E2.80.9337_59-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoward200436.E2.80.9337-59"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBogdanovWoodstraErlewine2002508_69-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBogdanovWoodstraErlewine2002508-69"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup>
Regarded
by
many
as
his
best
work,
the
album
topped
the
charts
on
both
sides
of
the
Atlantic.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBogdanovWoodstraErlewine2002181_70-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBogdanovWoodstraErlewine2002181-70"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInglis2010xv.2C_23_71-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInglis2010xv.2C_23-71"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-73"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>nb
5<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
LP
produced
the
number-one
<a
href="/wiki/Hit_single?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hit
single">hit
single</a>
&quot;My
Sweet
Lord&quot;
and
the
top-ten
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/What_Is_Life?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="What
Is
Life">What
Is
Life</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoberts2005227_74-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoberts2005227-74"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
was
co-produced
by
<a
href="/wiki/Phil_Spector?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Phil
Spector">Phil
Spector</a>
using
his
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Wall_of_Sound?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wall
of
Sound">Wall
of
Sound</a>&quot;
approach,<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchaffner1978142_75-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchaffner1978142-75"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
the
musicians
included
Starr,
Clapton,
<a
href="/wiki/Gary_Wright?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gary
Wright">Gary
Wright</a>,
Preston,
<a
href="/wiki/Klaus_Voormann?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Klaus
Voormann">Klaus
Voormann</a>,
the
whole
of
Delaney
and
Bonnie's
Friends
band
and
the
Apple
group
<a
href="/wiki/Badfinger?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Badfinger">Badfinger</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoward200436.E2.80.9337_59-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoward200436.E2.80.9337-59"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng200678_76-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng200678-76"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-78"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>nb
6<span>]</span></a></sup>
Ben
Gerson
of
<i>Rolling
Stone</i>
described
<i>All
Things
Must
Pass</i>
as
being
&quot;of
classic
Spectorian
proportions,
<a
href="/wiki/Richard_Wagner?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Richard
Wagner">Wagnerian</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Anton_Bruckner?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Anton
Bruckner">Brucknerian</a>,
the
music
of
mountain
tops
and
vast
horizons.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-Gerson_79-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Gerson-79"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup>
Author
and
<a
href="/wiki/Musicology?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Musicology">musicologist</a>
Ian
Inglis
considered
the
lyrics
of
<a
href="/wiki/All_Things_Must_Pass_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="All
Things
Must
Pass
(song)">the
album's
title
track</a>
&quot;a
recognition
of
the
impermanence
of
human
existence&nbsp;...
a
simple
and
poignant
conclusion&quot;
to
Harrison's
former
band.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInglis201030_80-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInglis201030-80"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1971
Bright
Tunes
sued
Harrison
for
<a
href="/wiki/Copyright_infringement?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Copyright
infringement">copyright
infringement</a>
over
&quot;My
Sweet
Lord&quot;
owing
to
its
similarity
to
the
1963
<a
href="/wiki/The_Chiffons?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Chiffons">Chiffons</a>
hit
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/He%27s_So_Fine?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="He's
So
Fine">He's
So
Fine</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoggett2009147.E2.80.93148_81-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoggett2009147.E2.80.93148-81"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
denied
deliberately
plagiarizing
the
song,
but
lost
the
court
case
in
1976
as
the
judge
ruled
that
he
had
done
so
subconsciously.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoggett2009251.E2.80.93252_82-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoggett2009251.E2.80.93252-82"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
2000
Apple
Records
released
a
thirtieth
anniversary
edition
of
the
album
and
Harrison
actively
participated
in
its
promotion,
giving
an
interview
during
which
he
reflected
on
the
work:
&quot;It's
just
something
that
was
like
my
continuation
from
the
Beatles,
really.
It
was
me
sort
of
getting
out
of
the
Beatles
and
just
going
my
own
way&nbsp;...
it
was
a
very
happy
occasion.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry200316_83-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry200316-83"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
commented
on
the
production:
&quot;Well,
in
those
days
it
was
like
the
<a
href="/wiki/Reverberation?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Reverberation">reverb</a>
was
kind
of
used
a
bit
more
than
what
I
would
do
now.
In
fact,
I
don't
use
reverb
at
all.
I
can't
stand
it&nbsp;...
You
know,
it's
hard
to
go
back
to
anything
thirty
years
later
and
expect
it
to
be
how
you
would
want
it
now.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry200312.E2.80.9313_84-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry200312.E2.80.9313-84"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="The_Concert_for_Bangladesh">The
Concert
for
Bangladesh</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=George_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6"
title="Edit
section:
The
Concert
for
Bangladesh">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="rellink
relarticle
mainarticle">








Main
article:









<a
href="/wiki/The_Concert_for_Bangladesh?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Concert
for
Bangladesh">The
Concert
for
Bangladesh</a>







</div>








<p>Responding
to
a
request
from
Ravi
Shankar,
Harrison
organized
a
charity
event,
the
Concert
for
Bangladesh,
which
took
place
on
1
August
1971,
drawing
over
40,000
people
to
two
shows
in
New
York's
<a
href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Madison
Square
Garden">Madison
Square
Garden</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-ConcertforBangladesh_85-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ConcertforBangladesh-85"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
goal
of
the
event
was
to
raise
money
to
aid
starving
refugees
during
the
<a
href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Liberation_War?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bangladesh
Liberation
War">Bangladesh
Liberation
War</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2003132.E2.80.93136_86-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2003132.E2.80.93136-86"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup>
Shankar
opened
the
show,
which
featured
popular
musicians
such
as
Dylan,
Clapton,
<a
href="/wiki/Leon_Russell?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Leon
Russell">Leon
Russell</a>,
Badfinger,
Preston
and
Starr.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2003132.E2.80.93136_86-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2003132.E2.80.93136-86"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>A
triple
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Concert_for_Bangladesh_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Concert
for
Bangladesh
(album)">The
Concert
for
Bangladesh</a></i>,
was
released
by
<a
href="/wiki/Apple_Corps?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Apple
Corps">Apple
Corps</a>
that
year,
followed
by
a
<a
href="/wiki/The_Concert_for_Bangladesh_(film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Concert
for
Bangladesh
(film)">concert
film</a>
in
1972.
Tax
troubles
and
questionable
expenses
later
tied
up
many
of
the
proceeds,
but
Harrison
commented:
&quot;Mainly
the
concert
was
to
attract
attention
to
the
situation&nbsp;...
The
money
we
raised
was
secondary,
and
although
we
had
some
money
problems&nbsp;...
they
still
got
plenty&nbsp;...
even
though
it
was
a
drop
in
the
ocean.
The
main
thing
was,
we
spread
the
word
and
helped
get
the
war
ended.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-87"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
event
has
been
described
as
an
innovative
precursor
for
the
large-scale
charity
rock
shows
that
followed,
including
<a
href="/wiki/Live_Aid?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Live
Aid">Live
Aid</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2003135_88-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2003135-88"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-90"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>nb
7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Living_in_the_Material_World_to_George_Harrison"><i>Living
in
the
Material
World</i>
to
<i>George
Harrison</i></span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=George_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7"
title="Edit
section:
Living
in
the
Material
World
to
George
Harrison">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p><i><a
href="/wiki/Living_in_the_Material_World?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Living
in
the
Material
World">Living
in
the
Material
World</a></i>
(1973)
held
the
number
one
spot
on
the
<i>Billboard</i>
album
chart
for
five
weeks,
and
the
album's
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Give_Me_Love_(Give_Me_Peace_on_Earth)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Give
Me
Love
(Give
Me
Peace
on
Earth)">Give
Me
Love
(Give
Me
Peace
on
Earth)</a>&quot;,
also
reached
number
one
in
the
US.<sup
id="cite_ref-91"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
the
UK,
the
LP
achieved
number
two,
spending
12
weeks
on
the
charts
with
the
single
peaking
at
number
8.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoberts2005227_74-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoberts2005227-74"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
was
lavishly
produced
and
packaged,
and
its
dominant
message
was
Harrison's
Hindu
beliefs.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchaffner1978158.E2.80.93159_92-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchaffner1978158.E2.80.93159-92"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
Greene's
opinion
it
&quot;contained
many
of
the
strongest
compositions
of
his
career&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGreene2006194_93-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGreene2006194-93"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Rolling
Stone</i><span
style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s
<a
href="/wiki/Stephen_Holden?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stephen
Holden">Stephen
Holden</a>
declared
the
album
&quot;vastly
appealing&quot;
and
&quot;profoundly
seductive&nbsp;...
[it]
stands
alone
as
an
article
of
faith,
miraculous
in
its
radiance.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng2006195_94-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng2006195-94"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup>
Other
reviewers
were
less
enthusiastic,
describing
the
release
as
awkward,
sanctimonious
and
overly
sentimental,
a
reaction
that
left
Harrison
despondent.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInglis201043.2C_46_95-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInglis201043.2C_46-95"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
November
1974
Harrison
began
his
45-date
Dark
Horse
Tour,
becoming
the
first
ex-Beatle
to
tour
North
America.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng2006166.2C_195_96-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng2006166.2C_195-96"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
addition
to
performances
by
Harrison
with
an
ensemble
of
musicians
such
as
Preston,
<a
href="/wiki/Tom_Scott_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tom
Scott
(musician)">Tom
Scott</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Willie_Weeks?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Willie
Weeks">Willie
Weeks</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Andy_Newmark?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Andy
Newmark">Andy
Newmark</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Jim_Horn?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jim
Horn">Jim
Horn</a>,
the
tour
also
included
traditional
and
contemporary
Indian
music
performed
by
&quot;Ravi
Shankar,
Family
and
Friends&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-97"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup>
Despite
numerous
positive
reviews
the
consensus
reaction
to
the
tour
was
negative,
with
complaints
about
the
content,
structure,
and
length;
the
show's
duration
of
two
and
a
half
hours
was
seen
as
excessive
at
the
time.<sup
id="cite_ref-98"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup>
Some
fans
found
Shankar's
significant
presence
a
bizarre
disappointment,
having
expected
to
see
only
Harrison
perform,
and
many
were
affronted
by
what
Inglis
described
as
Harrison's
&quot;sermonizing&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInglis201049_99-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInglis201049-99"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup>
Further,
he
reworked
the
lyrics
to
several
Beatles
songs,
and
some
of
the
substitutions
were
seen
as
&quot;gratuitously
offensive&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInglis201049_99-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInglis201049-99"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup>
His
<a
href="/wiki/Laryngitis?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Laryngitis">laryngitis</a>-affected
vocals
also
disappointed
fans
and
critics,
who
began
calling
the
tour
&quot;dark
hoarse&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-100"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup>
Harrison
was
so
deeply
bothered
by
the
caustic
backlash
that
he
did
not
tour
again
until
the
1990s.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInglis201049_99-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInglis201049-99"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
author
Robert
Rodriguez
commented:
&quot;While
the
Dark
Horse
tour
might
be
considered
a
noble
failure,
there
were
a
number
of
fans
who
were
tuned-in
to
what
was
being
attempted.
They
went
away
ecstatic,
conscious
that
they
had
just
witnessed
something
so
uplifting
that
it
could
never
be
repeated.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERodriguez2010258_101-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERodriguez2010258-101"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup>
Leng
called
the
tour
&quot;groundbreaking&quot;
and
&quot;revolutionary
in
its
presentation
of
Indian
Music&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng2006173.2C_177_102-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng2006173.2C_177-102"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
December
Harrison
released
<i><a
href="/wiki/Dark_Horse_(George_Harrison_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dark
Horse
(George
Harrison
album)">Dark
Horse</a></i>,
an
album
that
earned
him
the
least
favourable
reviews
of
his
career.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGreene2006213_103-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGreene2006213-103"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Rolling
Stone</i>
called
it
&quot;the
chronicle
of
a
performer
out
of
his
element,
working
to
a
deadline,
enfeebling
his
overtaxed
talents
by
a
rush
to
deliver
a
new
'LP
product',
rehearse
a
band,
and
assemble
a
cross-country
tour,
all
within
three
weeks.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuntley2006114_104-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuntley2006114-104"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
reached
number
4
on
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Billboard_magazine?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
magazine"
class="mw-redirect">Billboard</a></i>
chart
and
the
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Dark_Horse_(George_Harrison_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dark
Horse
(George
Harrison
song)">Dark
Horse</a>&quot;
reached
number
15,
but
they
failed
to
make
an
impact
in
the
UK.<sup
id="cite_ref-105"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-106"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>nb
8<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
music
critic
<a
href="/wiki/Mikal_Gilmore?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mikal
Gilmore">Mikal
Gilmore</a>
described
<i>Dark
Horse</i>
as
&quot;one
of
Harrison's
most
fascinating
works
–
a
record
about
change
and
loss&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilmore200246_107-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilmore200246-107"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Harrison's
final
studio
album
for
EMI
and
Apple
Records
was
the
<a
href="/wiki/Soul_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Soul
music">soul
music</a>-inspired
<i><a
href="/wiki/Extra_Texture_(Read_All_About_It)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Extra
Texture
(Read
All
About
It)">Extra
Texture
(Read
All
About
It)</a></i>
(1975).<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng2006180_108-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng2006180-108"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
considered
it
the
least
satisfactory
of
the
three
he
had
recorded
since
<i>All
Things
Must
Pass</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInglis201054.E2.80.9355_109-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInglis201054.E2.80.9355-109"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup>
Leng
identified
&quot;bitterness
and
dismay&quot;
in
many
of
the
album's
tracks;
his
long-time
friend
Klaus
Voormann
commented:
&quot;He
wasn't
up
for
it&nbsp;...
It
was
a
terrible
time
because
I
think
there
was
a
lot
of
cocaine
going
around,
and
that's
when
I
got
out
of
the
picture&nbsp;...
I
didn't
like
his
frame
of
mind&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng2006179_110-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng2006179-110"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
released
two
singles
from
the
LP:
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/You_(George_Harrison_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="You
(George
Harrison
song)">You</a>&quot;,
which
reached
the
<i>Billboard</i>
top
20,
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/This_Guitar_(Can%27t_Keep_from_Crying)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="This
Guitar
(Can't
Keep
from
Crying)">This
Guitar
(Can't
Keep
from
Crying)</a>&quot;,
Apple's
final
original
single
release.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchaffner1978209.E2.80.93210_111-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchaffner1978209.E2.80.93210-111"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p><i><a
href="/wiki/Thirty_Three_%26_1/3?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Thirty
Three
&amp;
1/3">Thirty
Three
&amp;
1/3</a></i>
(1976),
Harrison's
first
album
release
on
his
own
Dark
Horse
Records
label,
produced
the
hit
singles
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/This_Song?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="This
Song">This
Song</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Crackerbox_Palace?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Crackerbox
Palace">Crackerbox
Palace</a>&quot;,
both
of
which
reached
the
top
25
in
the
US.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng2006187_112-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng2006187-112"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-115"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>nb
9<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
<a
href="/wiki/Surreal_humour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Surreal
humour">surreal
humour</a>
of
&quot;Crackerbox
Palace&quot;
reflected
Harrison's
association
with
<a
href="/wiki/Monty_Python?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Monty
Python">Monty
Python</a>'s
<a
href="/wiki/Eric_Idle?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Eric
Idle">Eric
Idle</a>,
who
directed
a
comical
music
video
for
the
song.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchaffner1978192_116-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchaffner1978192-116"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup>
With
an
emphasis
on
melody
and
musicianship,
and
a
more
subtle
subject
matter
than
the
pious
message
of
his
earlier
works,
<i>Thirty
Three
&amp;
1/3</i>
earned
Harrison
his
most
favourable
critical
notices
in
the
US
since
<i>All
Things
Must
Pass</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchaffner1978192_116-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchaffner1978192-116"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-118"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>nb
10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
1979,
following
his
second
marriage
and
the
birth
of
his
son
<a
href="/wiki/Dhani_Harrison?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dhani
Harrison">Dhani</a>,
he
released
<i><a
href="/wiki/George_Harrison_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="George
Harrison
(album)">George
Harrison</a></i>.
The
album
and
the
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Blow_Away?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blow
Away">Blow
Away</a>&quot;
both
made
the
<i>Billboard</i>
top
20.<sup
id="cite_ref-119"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
marked
the
beginning
of
Harrison's
gradual
retreat
from
the
music
business,
and
the
fruition
of
ideas
introduced
on
<i>All
Things
Must
Pass</i>.
In
1978
the
death
of
his
father
in
May
and
the
birth
of
his
son
in
August
had
influenced
his
decision
to
devote
more
time
to
his
family
than
to
his
career.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng2006210_120-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng2006210-120"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup>
Leng
described
the
album
as
&quot;melodic
and
lush&nbsp;...
peaceful&nbsp;...
the
work
of
a
man
who
had
lived
the
rock
and
roll
dream
twice
over
and
was
now
embracing
domestic
as
well
as
spiritual
bliss.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng2006210_120-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng2006210-120"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

charity

playing
&quot;










<a

title="Here
