<p>The
<a
href="/wiki/Death_of_John_Lennon?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Death
of
John
Lennon">murder
of
Lennon</a>
on
8
December
1980
disturbed
Harrison
and
reinforced
his
decades-long
concerns
about
<a
href="/wiki/Stalking?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stalking">stalkers</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2003247_121-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2003247-121"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
was
also
a
deep
personal
loss,
although
unlike
McCartney
and
Starr,
Harrison
had
had
little
contact
with
Lennon
in
the
years
before
his
death.<sup
id="cite_ref-Doggett_2009_265.E2.80.93266_122-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Doggett_2009_265.E2.80.93266-122"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-123"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>nb
11<span>]</span></a></sup>
Following
the
murder,
Harrison
commented:
&quot;After
all
we
went
through
together
I
had
and
still
have
great
love
and
respect
for
John
Lennon.
I
am
shocked
and
stunned.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2003247_121-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2003247-121"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Harrison
modified
the
lyrics
of
a
song
he
had
written
for
Starr
to
make
it
a
tribute
song
to
Lennon.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoggett2009273_124-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoggett2009273-124"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/All_Those_Years_Ago?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="All
Those
Years
Ago">All
Those
Years
Ago</a>&quot;,
which
included
vocal
contributions
from
Paul
and
Linda
McCartney,
as
well
as
Starr's
original
drum
part,
peaked
at
number
two
in
the
US
charts.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGeorge-Warren2001414_125-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGeorge-Warren2001414-125"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry200317.E2.80.9318_126-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry200317.E2.80.9318-126"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
single
was
included
on
the
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Somewhere_in_England?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Somewhere
in
England">Somewhere
in
England</a></i>
in
1981.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry200317.E2.80.9318.2C_349.E2.80.93350.2C_367_127-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry200317.E2.80.9318.2C_349.E2.80.93350.2C_367-127"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup>
Harrison
did
not
release
any
new
albums
for
five
years
after
1982's
<i><a
href="/wiki/Gone_Troppo?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gone
Troppo">Gone
Troppo</a></i>
received
little
notice
from
critics
or
the
public.<sup
id="cite_ref-128"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>During
this
period
he
made
several
guest
appearances,
including
a
1985
performance
at
a
tribute
to
<a
href="/wiki/Carl_Perkins?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Carl
Perkins">Carl
Perkins</a>
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Blue_Suede_Shoes:_A_Rockabilly_Session?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blue
Suede
Shoes:
A
Rockabilly
Session">Blue
Suede
Shoes:
A
Rockabilly
Session</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoggett2009287_129-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoggett2009287-129"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-131"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>nb
12<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
March
1986
he
made
a
surprise
appearance
during
the
finale
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Heart_Beat_86?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Heart
Beat
86">Birmingham
Heart
Beat
Charity
Concert</a>,
an
event
organized
to
raise
money
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/Heart_Beat_86?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Heart
Beat
86">Birmingham
Children's
Hospital</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBadman2001368_132-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBadman2001368-132"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
following
year,
he
appeared
at
<a
href="/wiki/The_Prince%27s_Trust?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Prince's
Trust">The
Prince's
Trust</a>
concert
at
London's
<a
href="/wiki/Wembley_Arena?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wembley
Arena">Wembley
Arena</a>,
performing
&quot;While
My
Guitar
Gently
Weeps&quot;
and
&quot;Here
Comes
the
Sun&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuntley2006202.E2.80.93203_133-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuntley2006202.E2.80.93203-133"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
February
1987
he
joined
Dylan,
<a
href="/wiki/John_Fogerty?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Fogerty">John
Fogerty</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Jesse_Ed_Davis?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jesse
Ed
Davis">Jesse
Ed
Davis</a>
on
stage
for
a
two-hour
performance
with
the
blues
musician
<a
href="/wiki/Taj_Mahal_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Taj
Mahal
(musician)">Taj
Mahal</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBadman2001386_134-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBadman2001386-134"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup>
Harrison
recalled:
&quot;Bob
rang
me
up
and
asked
if
I
wanted
to
come
out
for
the
evening
and
see
Taj
Mahal&nbsp;...
So
we
went
there
and
had
a
few
of
these
Mexican
beers
–
and
had
a
few
more&nbsp;...
Bob
says,
'Hey,
why
don't
we
all
get
up
and
play,
and
you
can
sing?'
But
every
time
I
got
near
the
microphone,
Dylan
comes
up
and
just
starts
singing
this
rubbish
in
my
ear,
trying
to
throw
me.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry200392_135-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry200392-135"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
November
1987
Harrison
released
the
platinum
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Cloud_Nine_(George_Harrison_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cloud
Nine
(George
Harrison
album)">Cloud
Nine</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng2006251.E2.80.93253_136-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng2006251.E2.80.93253-136"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-137"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup>
Co-produced
with
<a
href="/wiki/Jeff_Lynne?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jeff
Lynne">Jeff
Lynne</a>
of
<a
href="/wiki/Electric_Light_Orchestra?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Electric
Light
Orchestra">Electric
Light
Orchestra</a>,
the
LP
included
Harrison's
rendition
of
<a
href="/wiki/James_Ray_(singer)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="James
Ray
(singer)">James
Ray's</a>
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Got_My_Mind_Set_on_You?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Got
My
Mind
Set
on
You">Got
My
Mind
Set
on
You</a>&quot;,
which
went
to
number
one
in
the
US
and
number
two
in
the
UK.<sup
id="cite_ref-Cloud9Awards_138-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Cloud9Awards-138"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-UKSingles_139-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-UKSingles-139"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
accompanying
music
video
received
substantial
airplay,<sup
id="cite_ref-140"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
another
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/When_We_Was_Fab?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="When
We
Was
Fab">When
We
Was
Fab</a>&quot;,
a
retrospective
of
the
Beatles'
career,
earned
two
<a
href="/wiki/MTV_Music_Video_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Music
Video
Award"
class="mw-redirect">MTV
Music
Video
Awards</a>
nominations
in
1988.<sup
id="cite_ref-141"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup>
Recorded
at
his
estate
in
Friar
Park,
Harrison's
slide
guitar
playing
featured
prominently
on
the
album,
which
included
several
of
his
long-time
musical
collaborators,
including
Clapton,
Keltner,
and
Jim
Horn,
who
recalled
Harrison's
relaxed
and
friendly
demeanour
during
the
sessions:
&quot;George
made
you
feel
at
home,
in
his
home&nbsp;...
He
once
had
me
sit
on
a
toilet
and
play
my
<a
href="/wiki/Soprano_saxophone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Soprano
saxophone">soprano
sax</a>,
and
they
miked
it
at
the
end
of
the
hall
for
a
distant
sound.
I
thought
they
were
kidding&nbsp;...
Another
time
he
stopped
me
in
the
middle
of
a
sax
solo
and
brought
me
3
p.m.
tea—again
I
thought
he
was
kidding.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng2006246.E2.80.93247_142-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng2006246.E2.80.93247-142"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Cloud
Nine</i>
reached
number
eight
and
number
ten
on
the
US
and
UK
charts
respectively,
and
several
tracks
from
the
album
achieved
placement
on
<i>Billboard</i><span
style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s
Mainstream
Rock
chart
–
&quot;Devil's
Radio&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/This_Is_Love_(George_Harrison_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="This
Is
Love
(George
Harrison
song)">This
Is
Love</a>&quot;
and
&quot;Cloud
9&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Cloud9Awards_138-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Cloud9Awards-138"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="1988.E2.80.932001:_later_life">1988–2001:
later
life</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=George_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9"
title="Edit
section:
1988–2001:
later
life">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="The_Traveling_Wilburys">The
Traveling
Wilburys</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=George_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10"
title="Edit
section:
The
Traveling
Wilburys">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="rellink
relarticle
mainarticle">








Main
article:









<a
href="/wiki/Traveling_Wilburys?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Traveling
Wilburys">Traveling
Wilburys</a>







</div>








<p>In
1988
Harrison
formed
the
Traveling
Wilburys
with
Jeff
Lynne,
<a
href="/wiki/Roy_Orbison?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Roy
Orbison">Roy
Orbison</a>,
Bob
Dylan
and
Tom
Petty.
The
band
had
gathered
in
Dylan's
garage
to
record
a
song
for
a
Harrison
European
single
release.<sup
id="cite_ref-143"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup>
Harrison's
record
company
decided
the
track,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Handle_with_Care_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Handle
with
Care
(song)">Handle
with
Care</a>&quot;,
was
too
good
for
its
original
purpose
as
a
B-side
and
asked
for
a
full
album.
The
LP,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Traveling_Wilburys_Vol._1?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Traveling
Wilburys
Vol.
1">Traveling
Wilburys
Vol.
1</a></i>,
was
released
in
October
1988
and
recorded
under
pseudonyms
as
half-brothers,
supposed
sons
of
Charles
Truscott
Wilbury,
Sr.<sup
id="cite_ref-144"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup>
Harrison's
pseudonym
on
the
first
album
was
&quot;Nelson
Wilbury&quot;;
he
used
the
name
&quot;Spike
Wilbury&quot;
for
their
second
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng2006267_145-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng2006267-145"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>After
Orbison's
death
in
December
1988
the
group
recorded
as
a
four-piece.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2003379_146-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2003379-146"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup>
Their
second
release,
issued
in
October
1990,
was
mischievously
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Traveling_Wilburys_Vol._3?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Traveling
Wilburys
Vol.
3">Traveling
Wilburys
Vol.
3</a></i>.
According
to
Lynne,
&quot;That
was
George's
idea.
He
said,
'Let's
confuse
the
buggers.'&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-147"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
reached
number
14
in
the
UK,
where
it
went
<a
href="/wiki/RIAA_certification?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="RIAA
certification">platinum</a>
with
certified
sales
of
more
than
3,000,000
units.<sup
id="cite_ref-148"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
Wilburys
never
performed
live
and
the
group
did
not
record
together
again
following
the
release
of
their
second
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-149"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
1989
Harrison
and
Starr
appeared
in
the
music
video
for
Tom
Petty's
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Won%27t_Back_Down?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Won't
Back
Down">I
Won't
Back
Down</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry200398_150-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry200398-150"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup>
Starr
is
filmed
playing
the
drums,
but
did
not
play
on
the
track;
Harrison
played
acoustic
guitar
and
provided
backing
vocals.<sup
id="cite_ref-151"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-154"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>nb
13<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
December
1991,
Harrison
joined
Clapton
for
a
tour
of
Japan.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2003374.E2.80.93375_155-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2003374.E2.80.93375-155"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
was
Harrison's
first
since
1974
and
no
others
followed.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2003374.E2.80.93378_156-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2003374.E2.80.93378-156"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-158"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>nb
14<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
6
April
1992,
Harrison
held
a
benefit
concert
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/Natural_Law_Party?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Natural
Law
Party">Natural
Law
Party</a>
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Royal
Albert
Hall">Royal
Albert
Hall</a>,
his
first
London
performance
since
<a
href="/wiki/The_Beatles%27_rooftop_concert?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Beatles'
rooftop
concert">the
Beatles'
1969
rooftop
concert</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-159"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-159"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
October
1992
he
performed
at
a
Bob
Dylan
tribute
concert
at
<a
href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Madison
Square
Garden">Madison
Square
Garden</a>
in
New
York
City,
playing
alongside
Dylan,
Clapton,
McGuinn,
Petty
and
<a
href="/wiki/Neil_Young?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Neil
Young">Neil
Young</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-160"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-160"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="The_Beatles_Anthology"><i>The
Beatles
Anthology</i></span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=George_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11"
title="Edit
section:
The
Beatles
Anthology">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="rellink
relarticle
mainarticle">








Main
article:









<a
href="/wiki/The_Beatles_Anthology?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Beatles
Anthology">The
Beatles
Anthology</a>







</div>








<p>In
1994
Harrison
began
a
collaboration
with
McCartney,
Starr
and
producer
Jeff
Lynne
for
the
<i>Beatles
Anthology</i>
project.
This
included
the
recording
of
two
new
Beatles
songs
built
around
solo
vocal
and
piano
tapes
recorded
by
Lennon
as
well
as
lengthy
interviews
about
the
Beatles'
career.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett1999286_161-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett1999286-161"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup>
Released
in
December
1995,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Free_as_a_Bird?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Free
as
a
Bird">Free
as
a
Bird</a>&quot;
was
the
first
new
Beatles
single
since
1970.<sup
id="cite_ref-162"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-162"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
March
1996,
they
released
a
second
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Real_Love_(The_Beatles_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Real
Love
(The
Beatles
song)">Real
Love</a>&quot;.
Harrison
refused
to
participate
in
the
completion
of
a
third
song.<sup
id="cite_ref-163"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-163"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
later
commented
on
the
project:
&quot;I
hope
somebody
does
this
to
all
my
crap
demos
when
I'm
dead,
make
them
into
hit
songs.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuntley2006259_164-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuntley2006259-164"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Following
the
<i>Anthology</i>
project,
Harrison
collaborated
with
Ravi
Shankar
on
the
latter's
<i><a
href="/wiki/Chants_of_India?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chants
of
India">Chants
of
India</a></i>.
Harrison's
final
television
appearance
was
a
<a
href="/wiki/VH1?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="VH1">VH-1</a>
special
to
promote
the
album,
taped
in
May
1997.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBadman2001568_165-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBadman2001568-165"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup>
Soon
after,
he
was
diagnosed
with
<a
href="/wiki/Head_and_neck_cancer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Head
and
neck
cancer">throat
cancer</a>,
and
treated
with
<a
href="/wiki/Radiation_therapy?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Radiation
therapy">radiotherapy</a>,
which
was
thought
at
the
time
to
be
successful.<sup
id="cite_ref-NYTimes1299_166-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-NYTimes1299-166"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
January
1998,
Harrison
attended
Carl
Perkins's
funeral
in
<a
href="/wiki/Jackson,_Tennessee?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jackson,
Tennessee">Jackson,
Tennessee</a>,
performing
a
brief
rendition
of
Perkins's
song
&quot;Your
True
Love&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBadman2001586_167-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBadman2001586-167"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
June
1998,
he
attended
the
public
memorial
service
for
<a
href="/wiki/Linda_McCartney?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Linda
McCartney">Linda
McCartney</a>,
and
appeared
on
Starr's
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Vertical_Man?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Vertical
Man">Vertical
Man</a></i>,
playing
guitar
on
two
tracks.<sup
id="cite_ref-168"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-168"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Knife_attack_and_illness">Knife
attack
and
illness</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=George_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12"
title="Edit
section:
Knife
attack
and
illness">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>On
30
December
1999,
36-year-old
Michael
Abram
broke
into
the
Harrisons'
<a
href="/wiki/Friar_Park?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Friar
Park">Friar
Park</a>
home
and
attacked
Harrison
with
a
kitchen
knife,
puncturing
a
lung
and
causing
head
injuries
before
Olivia
Harrison
incapacitated
the
assailant
by
striking
him
repeatedly
with
a
<a
href="/wiki/Fire_iron?qsrc=3044#Types_of_fire_irons"
title="Fire
iron">poker</a>
and
a
lamp.<sup
id="cite_ref-NYTimes1299_166-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-NYTimes1299-166"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIdle2005277.E2.80.93278_169-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIdle2005277.E2.80.93278-169"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup>
Following
the
attack,
Harrison
was
hospitalized
with
more
than
forty
stab
wounds.
He
released
a
statement
soon
after
regarding
his
assailant:
&quot;[he]
wasn't
a
burglar,
and
he
certainly
wasn't
auditioning
for
the
Traveling
Wilburys.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoggett2009328_170-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoggett2009328-170"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-174"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-174"><span>[</span>nb
15<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
May
2001
it
was
revealed
that
Harrison
had
undergone
an
operation
to
remove
a
cancerous
growth
from
one
of
his
lungs,<sup
id="cite_ref-175"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-175"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
in
July,
it
was
reported
that
he
was
being
treated
for
a
<a
href="/wiki/Brain_tumor?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brain
tumor">brain
tumour</a>
at
a
clinic
in
Switzerland.<sup
id="cite_ref-176"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-176"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup>
While
in
Switzerland,
Starr
visited
him,
but
had
to
cut
his
stay
short
to
travel
to
Los
Angeles,
where
his
daughter
was
undergoing
emergency
brain
surgery,
prompting
Harrison
to
quip:
&quot;Do
you
want
me
to
come
with
you?&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-177"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-177"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
November
2001,
he
began
radiotherapy
at
<a
href="/wiki/Staten_Island_University_Hospital?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Staten
Island
University
Hospital">Staten
Island
University
Hospital</a>
in
New
York
City
for
lung
cancer
that
had
<a
href="/wiki/Metastasis?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Metastasis">spread</a>
to
his
brain.<sup
id="cite_ref-178"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-178"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup>
When
the
news
was
publicized,
Harrison
bemoaned
his
physician's
breach
of
privacy,
and
his
estate
later
claimed
damages.<sup
id="cite_ref-184"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-184"><span>[</span>nb
16<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
12
November,
the
three
living
former
Beatles
met
for
the
last
time
at
Harrison's
hotel
in
New
York
for
lunch.<sup
id="cite_ref-185"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-185"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Death">Death</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=George_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13"
title="Edit
section:
Death">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>Harrison
died
on
29
November
2001,
aged
58,
from
<a
href="/wiki/Metastasis?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Metastasis">metastatic</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Lung_cancer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lung
cancer">non-small
cell
lung
cancer</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-186"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-186"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
was
<a
href="/wiki/Cremation?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cremation">cremated</a>
at
<a
href="/wiki/Hollywood_Forever_Cemetery?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hollywood
Forever
Cemetery">Hollywood
Forever
Cemetery</a>
and
his
ashes
were
scattered
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/Ganges?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ganges">Ganges</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Yamuna?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Yamuna">Yamuna</a>
Rivers
near
<a
href="/wiki/Varanasi?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Varanasi">Varanasi</a>,
India,
by
his
close
family
in
a
private
ceremony
according
to
<a
href="/wiki/Ganges_in_Hinduism?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ganges
in
Hinduism">Hindu
tradition</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-187"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-187"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
left
almost
&pound;100&nbsp;million
in
his
will.<sup
id="cite_ref-188"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-188"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>His
final
album,
the
posthumously
released
<i><a
href="/wiki/Brainwashed_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brainwashed
(album)">Brainwashed</a></i>
(2002),
was
completed
by
his
son
Dhani
and
Jeff
Lynne.<sup
id="cite_ref-189"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-189"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup>
Included
in
the
album's
liner
notes
is
a
quotation
from
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Bhagavad_Gita?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bhagavad
Gita">Bhagavad
Gita</a></i>:
&quot;There
never
was
a
time
when
you
or
I
did
not
exist.
Nor
will
there
be
any
future
when
we
shall
cease
to
be.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInglis2010118_190-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInglis2010118-190"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup>
A
media-only
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Stuck_Inside_a_Cloud?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stuck
Inside
a
Cloud">Stuck
Inside
a
Cloud</a>&quot;,
which
Leng
described
as
&quot;a
uniquely
candid
reaction
to
illness
and
mortality&quot;,
achieved
number
27
on
<i>Billboard</i><span
style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s
Adult
Contemporary
chart.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng2006300_191-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng2006300-191"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-192"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-192"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Any_Road?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Any
Road">Any
Road</a>&quot;,
released
in
May
2003,
reached
number
37
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="UK
Singles
Chart">UK
Singles
Chart</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-UKSingles_139-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-UKSingles-139"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;Marwa
Blues&quot;
went
on
to
receive
the
<a
href="/wiki/2004_Grammy_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="2004
Grammy
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">2004
Grammy
Award</a>
for
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Pop_Instrumental_Performance?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Best
Pop
Instrumental
Performance">Best
Pop
Instrumental
Performance</a>,
while
&quot;Any
Road&quot;
was
nominated
for
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Male_Pop_Vocal_Performance?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Best
Male
Pop
Vocal
Performance">Best
Male
Pop
Vocal
Performance</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-193"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-193"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Musicianship">Musicianship</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=George_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14"
title="Edit
section:
Musicianship">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Songwriting">Songwriting</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=George_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15"
title="Edit
section:
Songwriting">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="rellink
relarticle
mainarticle">








Main
article:









<a
href="/wiki/List_of_songs_recorded_by_George_Harrison?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="List
of
songs
recorded
by
George
Harrison">List
of
songs
recorded
by
George
Harrison</a>







</div>








<p>Harrison
wrote
his
first
song,
&quot;Don't
Bother
Me&quot;,
while
sick
in
a
hotel
bed
in
Bournemouth
during
August
1963,
as
&quot;an
exercise
to
see
if
I
<i>could</i>
write
a
song&quot;,
as
he
remembered.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarrison200284_194-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarrison200284-194"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;Don't
Bother
Me&quot;
appeared
on
the
band's
second
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/With_the_Beatles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="With
the
Beatles">With
the
Beatles</a></i>,
later
that
year,
then
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/Meet_the_Beatles!?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Meet
the
Beatles!">Meet
the
Beatles!</a></i>
in
the
US
in
early
1964.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2003159.E2.80.93160_195-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2003159.E2.80.93160-195"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1965,
he
contributed
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Need_You_(The_Beatles_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Need
You
(The
Beatles
song)">I
Need
You</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/You_Like_Me_Too_Much?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="You
Like
Me
Too
Much">You
Like
Me
Too
Much</a>&quot;
to
the
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Help!_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Help!
(album)">Help!</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000551:_.22I_Need_You.22.2C_1190:_.22You_Like_Me_Too_Much.22_196-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000551:_.22I_Need_You.22.2C_1190:_.22You_Like_Me_Too_Much.22-196"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInglis2010xv_197-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInglis2010xv-197"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Harrison's
songwriting
ability
improved
through
the
years,
but
his
material
did
not
earn
full
respect
from
his
fellow
Beatles
until
near
the
group's
break-up.
In
1969,
McCartney
told
Lennon:
&quot;Until
this
year,
our
songs
have
been
better
than
George's.
Now
this
year
his
songs
are
at
least
as
good
as
ours&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-198"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-198"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup>
Harrison
often
had
difficulty
getting
the
band
to
record
his
songs.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchinderSchwartz2008174_199-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchinderSchwartz2008174-199"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGeorge-Warren2001413_60-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGeorge-Warren2001413-60"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup>
Most
Beatles
albums
contain
at
least
two
Harrison
compositions,
and
there
are
three
of
his
songs
on
the
1966
<i><a
href="/wiki/Revolver_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Revolver
(album)"
class="mw-redirect">Revolver</a></i>
LP,
&quot;the
album
on
which
Harrison
came
of
age
as
a
songwriter&quot;,
wrote
Inglis.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInglis2010xv:_most_Beatles_albums_contain_at_least_two_Harrison_compositions.2C_7:.27.27Revolver.27.27_200-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInglis2010xv:_most_Beatles_albums_contain_at_least_two_Harrison_compositions.2C_7:.27.27Revolver.27.27-200"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

sample
of

Without

<td
colspan="2"
class="mbox-text"
style="line-height:1.1em;"><span
style="font-size:smaller;"><i>Problems
playing

<a

<p>Of
the
1967
Harrison
song
&quot;Within
You
Without
You&quot;,
author
Gerry
Farrell
claimed
that
Harrison
had
created
a
&quot;new
form&quot;,
calling
the
composition:
&quot;a
quintessential
fusion
of
pop
and
Indian
music.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng200631_201-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng200631-201"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup>
Lennon
called
the
song
one
of
Harrison's
best:
&quot;His
mind
and
his
music
are
clear.
There
is
his
innate
talent,
he
brought
that
sound
together.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_Beatles2000243_202-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_Beatles2000243-202"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup>
Beatles
biographer
Bob
Spitz
described
&quot;Something&quot;
as
a
masterpiece:
&quot;an
intensely
stirring
romantic
ballad
that
would
challenge
'Yesterday'
and
'Michelle'
as
one
of
the
most
recognizable
songs
they
ever
produced.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005837_203-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005837-203"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup>
According
to
Kenneth
Womack,
'Harrison
comes
into
his
own
on
<i>Abbey
Road</i>&nbsp;...
&quot;Here
Comes
the
Sun&quot;
is
matched—indeed,
surpassed—only
by
&quot;Something&quot;,
his
crowning
achievement'.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomack200689_204-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomack200689-204"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup>
Inglis
considered
<i>Abbey
Road</i>
a
turning
point
in
Harrison's
development
as
a
songwriter
and
musician.
He
described
Harrison's
contributions
to
the
LP
as
&quot;exquisite&quot;,
declaring
them
equal
to
any
previous
Beatles
songs.
During
the
album's
recording,
Harrison
asserted
more
creative
control
than
before,
proactively
rejecting
suggestions
for
changes
to
his
music
or
lyrics,
particularly
from
McCartney.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInglis201015_205-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInglis201015-205"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>His
interest
in
Indian
music
proved
a
strong
influence
on
his
songwriting
and
contributed
to
his
innovation
within
the
Beatles.
According
to
<i>Rolling
Stone</i>,
&quot;Harrison's
openness
to
new
sounds
and
textures
cleared
new
paths
for
his
rock
and
roll
compositions.
His
use
of
dissonance
on&nbsp;...
'Taxman'
and
'I
Want
to
Tell
You'
was
revolutionary
in
popular
music
–
and
perhaps
more
originally
creative
than
the
avant-garde
mannerisms
that
Lennon
and
McCartney
borrowed
from
the
music
of
<a
href="/wiki/Karlheinz_Stockhausen?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Karlheinz
Stockhausen">Karlheinz
Stockhausen</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Luciano_Berio?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Luciano
Berio">Luciano
Berio</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Edgard_Var%C3%A8se?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Edgard
Var&egrave;se">Edgard
Var&egrave;se</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Igor_Stravinsky?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Igor
Stravinsky">Igor
Stravinsky</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilmore200237_206-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilmore200237-206"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1997,
author
Gerry
Farrell
commented:
&quot;It
is
a
mark
of
Harrison's
sincere
involvement&nbsp;...
that,
nearly
thirty
years
on,
the
Beatles'
'Indian'
songs
remain
the
most
imaginative
and
successful
examples
of
this
type
of
fusion.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng2006316_207-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng2006316-207"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Guitar_work">Guitar
work</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=George_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16"
title="Edit
section:
Guitar
work">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="quotebox"
style="float:
right;
clear:
right;
margin:
0.5em
0
0.8em
1.4em;
width:
25em;
padding:
6px;
border:
1px
solid
#aaa;
font-size:
88%;
background-color:
#F9F9F9;
padding:8px;">









<div
style="position:
relative;
text-align:
left;">










<div>











<p>&quot;He
was
clearly
an
innovator:
George,
to
me,
was
taking
certain
elements
of
R&amp;B
and
rock
and
rockabilly
and
creating
something
unique.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarrison2011194_208-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarrison2011194-208"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup></p>










</div>









</div>









<div
style="text-align:
left;">









—Eric
Clapton








</div>








</div>








<p><i>Rolling
Stone</i>
founder
<a
href="/wiki/Jann_Wenner?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jann
Wenner">Jann
Wenner</a>
described
Harrison
as
&quot;a
guitarist
who
was
never
showy
but
who
had
an
innate,
eloquent
melodic
sense.
He
played
exquisitely
in
the
service
of
the
song&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarrison200215_209-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarrison200215-209"><span>[</span>193<span>]</span></a></sup>
Harrison's
friend
and
former
bandmate
Tom
Petty
agreed:
&quot;He
just
had
a
way
of
getting
right
to
the
business,
of
finding
the
right
thing
to
play.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPetty201158_210-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPetty201158-210"><span>[</span>194<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
<a
href="/wiki/Guitar_picking?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Guitar
picking">guitar
picking</a>
style
of
<a
href="/wiki/Chet_Atkins?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chet
Atkins">Chet
Atkins</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Carl_Perkins?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Carl
Perkins">Carl
Perkins</a>
influenced
Harrison,
giving
a
<a
href="/wiki/Country_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Country
music">country
music</a>
feel
to
many
of
the
Beatles'
recordings.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKitts200217_211-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKitts200217-211"><span>[</span>195<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
identified
<a
href="/wiki/Chuck_Berry?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chuck
Berry">Chuck
Berry</a>
as
an
early
influence
and
<a
href="/wiki/Ry_Cooder?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ry
Cooder">Ry
Cooder</a>
as
an
important
later
influence.<sup
id="cite_ref-212"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-212"><span>[</span>196<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
1961
the
Beatles
recorded
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Cry_for_a_Shadow?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cry
for
a
Shadow">Cry
for
a
Shadow</a>&quot;,
a
blues-inspired
instrumental
co-written
by
Lennon
and
Harrison,
who
is
credited
with
composing
the
song's
lead
guitar
part,
building
on
unusual
chord
voicings
and
imitating
the
style
of
other
English
groups
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/The_Shadows?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Shadows">the
Shadows</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng20064.E2.80.935_213-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng20064.E2.80.935-213"><span>[</span>197<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
musicologist
Walter
Everett
noted
that
while
early
Beatles
compositions
typically
held
close
to
the
conventional
patterns
in
rock
music
at
the
time,
he
also
identified
significant
variations
in
their
rhythm
and
tonal
direction.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett200148_214-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett200148-214"><span>[</span>198<span>]</span></a></sup>
Harrison's
liberal
use
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Diatonic_scale?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Diatonic
scale">diatonic
scale</a>
in
his
guitar
playing
reveals
the
influence
of
<a
href="/wiki/Buddy_Holly?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Buddy
Holly">Buddy
Holly</a>,
and
his
interest
in
Berry
inspired
him
to
compose
songs
based
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Blues_scale?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blues
scale">blues
scale</a>
while
incorporating
a
<a
href="/wiki/Rockabilly?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rockabilly">rockabilly</a>
feel
in
the
style
of
Perkins.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett199913_215-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett199913-215"><span>[</span>199<span>]</span></a></sup>
Within
this
framework
he
often
utilized
<a
href="/wiki/Syncopation?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Syncopation">syncopation</a>,
as
during
his
guitar
solos
for
the
Beatles'
covers
of
Berry's
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Roll_Over_Beethoven?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Roll
Over
Beethoven">Roll
Over
Beethoven</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Too_Much_Monkey_Business?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Too
Much
Monkey
Business">Too
Much
Monkey
Business</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett200162.E2.80.9363.2C_136_216-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett200162.E2.80.9363.2C_136-216"><span>[</span>200<span>]</span></a></sup>
Another
of
Harrison's
musical
techniques
was
the
use
of
guitar
lines
written
in
<a
href="/wiki/Octave?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Octave">octaves</a>,
as
on
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I%27ll_Be_on_My_Way?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I'll
Be
on
My
Way">I'll
Be
on
My
Way</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett2001134.E2.80.93135_217-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett2001134.E2.80.93135-217"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
was
the
first
person
to
own
a
<a
href="/wiki/Rickenbacker_360/12?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rickenbacker
360/12">Rickenbacker
360/12</a>,
a
guitar
that
featured
twelve
strings
in
6
pairs,
the
low
eight
of
which
are
tuned
in
pairs,
one
octave
apart;
the
higher
4
being
pairs
tuned
in
unison.
The
Rickenbacker
is
unique
among
twelve
string
guitars
in
having
the
lower
octave
string
of
each
of
the
first
four
pairs
placed
above
the
higher
tuned
string.
This,
and
the
naturally
rich
harmonics
produced
by
a
twelve
string
guitar
providing
the
distinctive
overtones
found
on
many
of
the
Beatles
recordings.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett2001134.E2.80.93135_217-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett2001134.E2.80.93135-217"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup>
His
use
of
this
guitar
during
the
recording
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/A_Hard_Day%27s_Night_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="A
Hard
Day's
Night
(album)">A
Hard
Day's
Night</a></i>
helped
to
popularize
the
model,
and
the
jangly
sound
became
so
prominent
that
<i><a
href="/wiki/Melody_Maker?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Melody
Maker">Melody
Maker</a></i>
termed
it
the
Beatles'
&quot;secret
weapon&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-218"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-218"><span>[</span>202<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-220"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-220"><span>[</span>nb
17<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Harrison
wrote
the
<a
href="/wiki/Chord_progression?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chord
progression">chord
progression</a>
of
his
first
published
song,
&quot;Don't
Bother
Me&quot;
(1963),
almost
exclusively
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/Dorian_mode?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dorian
mode">Dorian
mode</a>,
demonstrating
an
interest
in
exotic
tones
that
eventually
culminated
in
his
embrace
of
Indian
music.
The
dark
<a
href="/wiki/Timbre?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Timbre">timbre</a>
of
his
guitar
playing
on
the
track
was
accentuated
by
his
use
of
uncomplicated
yet
effective
C+9
<a
href="/wiki/Chord_(music)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chord
(music)">chord</a>
voicings
and
a
solo
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/Pentatonic_scale?qsrc=3044#Minor_pentatonic_scale"
title="Pentatonic
scale">minor
pentatonic
scale</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett2001193.E2.80.93195_221-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett2001193.E2.80.93195-221"><span>[</span>204<span>]</span></a></sup>
By
1964
he
had
begun
to
develop
a
distinctive
personal
style
as
a
guitarist,
writing
parts
that
featured
the
use
of
nonresolving
tones,
as
with
the
ending
chord
arpeggios
on
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/A_Hard_Day%27s_Night_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="A
Hard
Day's
Night
(song)">A
Hard
Day's
Night</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett199913_215-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett199913-215"><span>[</span>199<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1965
he
used
an
<a
href="/wiki/Expression_pedal?qsrc=3044#Guitars_and_digital_effects"
title="Expression
pedal">expression
pedal</a>
to
control
his
guitar's
volume
on
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Need_You_(The_Beatles_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Need
You
(The
Beatles
song)">I
Need
You</a>&quot;,
creating
a
syncopated
<a
href="/wiki/String_instrument?qsrc=3044#Contact_points_along_the_string"
title="String
instrument">flautando</a>
effect
with
the
melody
resolving
its
<a
href="/wiki/Consonance_and_dissonance?qsrc=3044#Dissonance"
title="Consonance
and
dissonance">dissonance</a>
through
tonal
displacements.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett2001284.E2.80.93285_222-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett2001284.E2.80.93285-222"><span>[</span>205<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
used
the
same
volume-swell
technique
on
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Yes_It_Is?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Yes
It
Is">Yes
It
Is</a>&quot;,
applying
what
Everett
described
as
&quot;ghostly
articulation&quot;
to
the
song's
<a
href="/wiki/Harmonic?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Harmonic">natural
harmonics</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett199913_215-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett199913-215"><span>[</span>199<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Of
<i>Rubber
Soul</i><span
style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/If_I_Needed_Someone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="If
I
Needed
Someone">If
I
Needed
Someone</a>&quot;,
Harrison
said:
&quot;it's
like
a
million
other
songs
written
around
the
D
chord.
If
you
move
your
fingers
about,
you
get
various
little
melodies&nbsp;...
it
amazes
me
that
people
still
find
new
permutations
of
the
same
notes.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett2001318_223-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett2001318-223"><span>[</span>206<span>]</span></a></sup>
His
other
contribution
to
the
album,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Think_for_Yourself?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Think
for
Yourself">Think
for
Yourself</a>&quot;,
features
what
Everett
described
as
&quot;ambiguous
tonal
coloring&quot;,
utilizing
<a
href="/wiki/Chromaticism?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chromaticism">chromaticism</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Major_chord?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Major
chord">G
major</a>
with
a
&quot;strange&quot;
mixture
of
the
Dorian
mode
and
the
minor
pentatonic;
he
called
it
a
&quot;tour
de
force
of
altered
scale
degrees&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-224"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-224"><span>[</span>207<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1966
Harrison
contributed
innovative
musical
ideas
to
<i>Revolver</i>.
He
played
<a
href="/wiki/Backmasking?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Backmasking">backwards</a>
guitar
on
Lennon's
composition
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I%27m_Only_Sleeping?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I'm
Only
Sleeping">I'm
Only
Sleeping</a>&quot;
and
a
guitar
<a
href="/wiki/Counter-melody?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Counter-melody">counter-melody</a>
on
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/And_Your_Bird_Can_Sing?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="And
Your
Bird
Can
Sing">And
Your
Bird
Can
Sing</a>&quot;
that
moved
in
parallel
octaves
above
McCartney's
bass
downbeats.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett199947.2C_49.E2.80.9351_225-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett199947.2C_49.E2.80.9351-225"><span>[</span>208<span>]</span></a></sup>
His
guitar
playing
on
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Want_to_Tell_You?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Want
to
Tell
You">I
Want
to
Tell
You</a>&quot;
exemplified
the
pairing
of
altered
chordal
colours
with
descending
chromatic
lines
and
his
guitar
part
for
<i>Sgt
Pepper's</i>
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Lucy_in_the_Sky_with_Diamonds?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lucy
in
the
Sky
with
Diamonds">Lucy
in
the
Sky
with
Diamonds</a>&quot;
mirrors
Lennon's
vocal
line
in
much
the
same
way
that
a
<a
href="/wiki/Sarangi?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sarangi">sarangi</a>
player
accompanies
a
<a
href="/wiki/Khyal?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Khyal">khyal</a>
singer
in
a
Hindu
<a
href="/wiki/Bhajan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bhajan">devotional
song</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-226"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-226"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>Everett
described
Harrison's
guitar
solo
from
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Old_Brown_Shoe?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Old
Brown
Shoe">Old
Brown
Shoe</a>&quot;
as
&quot;stinging
[and]
highly
Claptonesque&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett1999243_227-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett1999243-227"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
identified
two
of
the
composition's
significant
<a
href="/wiki/Motif_(music)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Motif
(music)">motifs</a>:
a
bluesy
<a
href="/wiki/Trichord?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Trichord">trichord</a>
and
a
<a
href="/wiki/Diminished_triad?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Diminished
triad">diminished
triad</a>
with
roots
in
A
and
E.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett1999244_228-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett1999244-228"><span>[</span>211<span>]</span></a></sup>
Huntley
called
the
song
&quot;a
sizzling
rocker
with
a
ferocious&nbsp;...
solo.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuntley200635_229-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuntley200635-229"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
Greene's
opinion,
Harrison's
demo
for
the
song
contains
&quot;one
of
the
most
complex
lead
guitar
solos
on
any
Beatles
song.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGreene2006140_230-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGreene2006140-230"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Harrison's
playing
on
<i>Abbey
Road</i>,
and
in
particular
on
&quot;Something&quot;,
marked
a
significant
moment
in
his
development
as
a
guitarist.
The
song's
guitar
solo
shows
a
varied
range
of
influences,
incorporating
the
blues
guitar
style
of
Clapton
and
the
styles
of
Indian
<a
href="/wiki/Gamaka_(music)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gamaka
(music)">gamakas</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng200642_231-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng200642-231"><span>[</span>214<span>]</span></a></sup>
According
to
author
and
musicologist
Kenneth
Womack:
&quot;'Something'
meanders
toward
the
most
unforgettable
of
Harrison's
guitar
solos&nbsp;...
A
masterpiece
in
simplicity,
[it]
reaches
toward
the
sublime&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomack200689_204-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomack200689-204"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup>
Harrison
received
an
Ivor
Novello
award
in
July
1970
for
&quot;Something&quot;,
as
&quot;The
Best
Song
Musically
and
Lyrically
of
the
Year&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBadman200112_232-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBadman200112-232"><span>[</span>215<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>After
<a
href="/wiki/Delaney_Bramlett?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Delaney
Bramlett">Delaney
Bramlett</a>
inspired
him
to
learn
slide
guitar,
Harrison
began
to
incorporate
it
into
his
solo
work,
which
allowed
him
to
mimic
many
traditional
Indian
instruments,
including
the
<a
href="/wiki/Sarangi?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sarangi">sarangi</a>
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Esraj?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Esraj">dilruba</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng200684.E2.80.9385_233-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng200684.E2.80.9385-233"><span>[</span>216<span>]</span></a></sup>
Leng
described
Harrison's
slide
guitar
solo
on
Lennon's
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/How_Do_You_Sleep%3F_(John_Lennon_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="How
Do
You
Sleep?
(John
Lennon
song)">How
Do
You
Sleep?&quot;</a>
as
a
departure
for
&quot;the
sweet
soloist
of
'Something'&quot;,
calling
his
playing
&quot;rightly
famed&nbsp;...
one
of
Harrison's
greatest
guitar
statements.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng2006109_234-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng2006109-234"><span>[</span>217<span>]</span></a></sup>
Lennon
commented:
&quot;That's
the
best
he's
ever
fucking
played
in
his
life.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng2006109_234-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng2006109-234"><span>[</span>217<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>A
<a
href="/wiki/Music_of_Hawaii?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Music
of
Hawaii">Hawaiian</a>
influence
is
notable
in
much
of
Harrison's
music,
ranging
from
his
slide
guitar
work
on
<i>Gone
Troppo</i>
(1982)
to
his
televised
performance
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Cab_Calloway?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cab
Calloway">Cab
Calloway</a>
standard
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Between_the_Devil_and_the_Deep_Blue_Sea_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Between
the
Devil
and
the
Deep
Blue
Sea
(song)">Between
the
Devil
and
the
Deep
Blue
Sea</a>&quot;
on
<a
href="/wiki/Ukulele?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ukulele">ukulele</a>
in
1992.<sup
id="cite_ref-235"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-235"><span>[</span>218<span>]</span></a></sup>
Lavezzoli
described
Harrison's
slide
playing
on
the
Grammy-winning
instrumental
&quot;Marwa
Blues&quot;
(2002)
as
demonstrating
Hawaiian
influences
while
comparing
the
melody
to
an
Indian
<a
href="/wiki/Sarod?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sarod">sarod</a>
or
<a
href="/wiki/Veena_(Instrument)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Veena
(Instrument)"
class="mw-redirect">veena</a>,
calling
it
&quot;yet
another
demonstration
of
Harrison's
unique
slide
approach&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006198_236-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006198-236"><span>[</span>219<span>]</span></a></sup>
Harrison
was
an
admirer
of
<a
href="/wiki/George_Formby?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="George
Formby">George
Formby</a>
and
a
member
of
the
Ukulele
Society
of
Great
Britain,
and
played
a
ukulele
solo
in
the
style
of
Formby
at
the
end
of
&quot;Free
as
a
Bird&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng2006279_237-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng2006279-237"><span>[</span>220<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
performed
at
a
Formby
convention
in
1991,
and
served
as
the
honorary
president
of
the
George
Formby
Appreciation
Society.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuntley2006149.2C_232_238-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuntley2006149.2C_232-238"><span>[</span>221<span>]</span></a></sup>
Harrison
played
bass
guitar
on
numerous
tracks,
including
the
Beatles'
songs
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Drive_My_Car?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Drive
My
Car">Drive
My
Car</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/She_Said_She_Said?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="She
Said
She
Said">She
Said
She
Said</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Golden_Slumbers?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Golden
Slumbers">Golden
Slumbers</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Birthday_(The_Beatles_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Birthday
(The
Beatles
song)">Birthday</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Honey_Pie?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Honey
Pie">Honey
Pie</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-239"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-239"><span>[</span>222<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
also
played
bass
on
several
solo
recordings,
including
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Faster_(George_Harrison_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Faster
(George
Harrison
song)">Faster</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Wake_Up_My_Love?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wake
Up
My
Love">Wake
Up
My
Love</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Bye_Bye_Love_(The_Everly_Brothers_song)?qsrc=3044#George_Harrison.27s_version"
title="Bye
Bye
Love
(The
Everly
Brothers
song)">Bye
Bye
Love</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng2006205:_.22Faster.22.2C_230:_.22Wake_Up_My_Love.22.2C_152:_.22Bye_Bye_Love.22_240-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng2006205:_.22Faster.22.2C_230:_.22Wake_Up_My_Love.22.2C_152:_.22Bye_Bye_Love.22-240"><span>[</span>223<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Guitars">Guitars</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=George_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17"
title="Edit
section:
Guitars">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>When
Harrison
joined
the
Quarrymen
in
1958
his
main
guitar
was
a
<a
href="/wiki/H%C3%B6fner?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="H&ouml;fner">H&ouml;fner</a>
President
Acoustic,
which
he
soon
traded
for
a
H&ouml;fner
Club
40
model.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBabiuk200218.E2.80.9319:_H.C3.B6fner_President_Acoustic.2C_22:_H.C3.B6fner_Club_40_model_241-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBabiuk200218.E2.80.9319:_H.C3.B6fner_President_Acoustic.2C_22:_H.C3.B6fner_Club_40_model-241"><span>[</span>224<span>]</span></a></sup>
His
first
solid-body
electric
guitar
was
a
Czech-built
<a
href="/wiki/Jolana?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jolana">Jolana</a>
Futurama/Grazioso.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBabiuk200225.E2.80.9327_242-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBabiuk200225.E2.80.9327-242"><span>[</span>225<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
guitars
he
used
on
early
recordings
were
mainly
<a
href="/wiki/Gretsch?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gretsch">Gretsch</a>
models,
played
through
a
<a
href="/wiki/Vox_AC30?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Vox
AC30">Vox
amplifier</a>,
including
a
<a
href="/wiki/Gretsch_6128?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gretsch
6128">Gretsch
Duo
Jet</a>
that
he
bought
secondhand
in
1961,
and
posed
with
on
the
album
cover
for
<i>Cloud
Nine</i>
(1987).<sup
id="cite_ref-243"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-243"><span>[</span>226<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
also
bought
a
Gretsch
Tennessean
and
a
Gretsch
Country
Gentleman,
which
he
played
on
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/She_Loves_You?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="She
Loves
You">She
Loves
You</a>&quot;,
and
during
the
Beatles'
1964
appearance
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Ed_Sullivan_Show?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Ed
Sullivan
Show">The
Ed
Sullivan
Show</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBacon200565_244-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBacon200565-244"><span>[</span>227<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBabiuk200252.E2.80.9355:_Gretsch_6128_Duo_Jet.3B_89.E2.80.9391.2C_99.E2.80.93101:_Gretsch_6122_Country_Gentleman.3B_105.E2.80.93106:_Gretsch_6119.E2.80.9362_Tennessee_Rose_245-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBabiuk200252.E2.80.9355:_Gretsch_6128_Duo_Jet.3B_89.E2.80.9391.2C_99.E2.80.93101:_Gretsch_6122_Country_Gentleman.3B_105.E2.80.93106:_Gretsch_6119.E2.80.9362_Tennessee_Rose-245"><span>[</span>228<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1963
he
bought
a
<a
href="/wiki/Rickenbacker?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rickenbacker">Rickenbacker</a>
425
Fireglo,
and
in
1964
he
acquired
a
Rickenbacker
360/12
guitar,
which
was
the
second
of
its
kind
to
be
manufactured.<sup
id="cite_ref-246"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-246"><span>[</span>229<span>]</span></a></sup>
Harrison
obtained
his
first
<a
href="/wiki/Fender_Stratocaster?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fender
Stratocaster">Fender
Stratocaster</a>
in
1965
and
used
it
in
recording
<i>Rubber
Soul</i>,
notably
on
the
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Nowhere_Man_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nowhere
Man
(song)">Nowhere
Man</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBabiuk2002157_247-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBabiuk2002157-247"><span>[</span>230<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
early
1966
Harrison,
Lennon,
and
McCartney
each
purchased
<a
href="/wiki/Epiphone_Casino?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Epiphone
Casino">Epiphone
Casinos</a>,
which
they
used
on
<i>Revolver</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBabiuk2002180.E2.80.93182.2C_198:_Epiphone_Casino_248-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBabiuk2002180.E2.80.93182.2C_198:_Epiphone_Casino-248"><span>[</span>231<span>]</span></a></sup>
Harrison
also
used
a
<a
href="/wiki/Gibson_J-160E?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gibson
J-160E">Gibson
J-160E</a>
and
a
<a
href="/wiki/Gibson_SG?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gibson
SG">Gibson
SG</a>
Standard
while
recording
the
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBabiuk200272.E2.80.9375:_Gibson_J-160E.2C_180.E2.80.93183:_Fender_Stratocaster_and_Gibson_SG_249-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBabiuk200272.E2.80.9375:_Gibson_J-160E.2C_180.E2.80.93183:_Fender_Stratocaster_and_Gibson_SG-249"><span>[</span>232<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
later
painted
his
Stratocaster
in
a
psychedelic
design
that
included
the
word
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Be-Bop-A-Lula?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Be-Bop-A-Lula">Bebopalula</a>&quot;
above
the
pickguard
and
the
guitar's
nickname,
&quot;Rocky&quot;,
on
the
headstock.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBabiuk2002156.E2.80.93157.2C_206.E2.80.93207:_Fender_Stratocaster_.22Rocky.22_250-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBabiuk2002156.E2.80.93157.2C_206.E2.80.93207:_Fender_Stratocaster_.22Rocky.22-250"><span>[</span>233<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
played
this
guitar
in
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Magical_Mystery_Tour_(film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Magical
Mystery
Tour
(film)">Magical
Mystery
Tour</a></i>
film
and
throughout
his
solo
career.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBabiuk2002224.E2.80.93225_251-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBabiuk2002224.E2.80.93225-251"><span>[</span>234<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
mid-1968
he
acquired
a
<a
href="/wiki/Gibson_Les_Paul?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gibson
Les
Paul">Gibson
Les
Paul</a>
that
he
nicknamed
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Lucy_(guitar)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lucy
(guitar)">Lucy</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBabiuk2002224.E2.80.93225:_Gibson_Les_Paul_.22.5B.5BLucy_.28guitar.29.7CLucy.5D.5D.22_252-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBabiuk2002224.E2.80.93225:_Gibson_Les_Paul_.22.5B.5BLucy_.28guitar.29.7CLucy.5D.5D.22-252"><span>[</span>235<span>]</span></a></sup>
Around
this
time,
he
obtained
a
Gibson
Jumbo
J-200,
which
he
used
for
early
demos
of
&quot;While
My
Guitar
Gently
Weeps&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBabiuk2002223.E2.80.93224:_Gibson_Jumbo_J-200_253-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBabiuk2002223.E2.80.93224:_Gibson_Jumbo_J-200-253"><span>[</span>236<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
late
1968
<a
href="/wiki/Fender_Musical_Instruments_Corporation?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fender
Musical
Instruments
Corporation">Fender
Musical
Instruments
Corporation</a>
gave
Harrison
a
custom-made
<a
href="/wiki/Fender_Telecaster?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fender
Telecaster">Fender
Telecaster</a>
Rosewood
prototype,
made
especially
for
him
by
a
Fender
master
builder
who
also
crafted
a
prototype
Stratocaster
for
<a
href="/wiki/Jimi_Hendrix?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jimi
Hendrix">Jimi
Hendrix</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBabiuk2002237.E2.80.93239:_Fender_Telecaster_254-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBabiuk2002237.E2.80.93239:_Fender_Telecaster-254"><span>[</span>237<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

See
also:









<a
href="/wiki/Apple_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Apple
