Records</a>&nbsp;and









<a
href="/wiki/Dark_Horse_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dark
Horse
Records">Dark
Horse
Records</a>







</div>








<p>Harrison's
music
projects
during
the
final
years
of
the
Beatles
included
producing
<a
href="/wiki/Apple_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Apple
Records">Apple
Records</a>
artists
<a
href="/wiki/Doris_Troy?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Doris
Troy">Doris
Troy</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Jackie_Lomax?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jackie
Lomax">Jackie
Lomax</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Billy_Preston?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billy
Preston">Billy
Preston</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng200655:_Lomax.3B_59:_Preston.3B_60.E2.80.9362:_Troy_255-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng200655:_Lomax.3B_59:_Preston.3B_60.E2.80.9362:_Troy-255"><span>[</span>238<span>]</span></a></sup>
Throughout
his
solo
career,
he
benefited
from
the
inclusion
of
guest
musicians
on
his
albums,
and
he
made
efforts
to
reciprocate
the
favours
by
participating
in
their
recordings.
He
was
featured
as
a
guitarist
on
tracks
by
<a
href="/wiki/Dave_Mason?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dave
Mason">Dave
Mason</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Nicky_Hopkins?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nicky
Hopkins">Nicky
Hopkins</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Alvin_Lee?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alvin
Lee">Alvin
Lee</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Ronnie_Wood?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ronnie
Wood">Ronnie
Wood</a>,
Billy
Preston
and
<a
href="/wiki/Tom_Scott_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tom
Scott
(musician)">Tom
Scott</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInglis201055_256-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInglis201055-256"><span>[</span>239<span>]</span></a></sup>
Harrison
co-wrote
songs
and
music
with
Dylan,
Clapton,
Preston,
Doris
Troy,
David
Bromberg,
Gary
Wright,
Wood,
Jeff
Lynne,
and
Tom
Petty,
among
others.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2003162.E2.80.93163:_Dylan.2C_121.E2.80.93125:_Eric_Clapton.2C_303.E2.80.93304:_Billy_Preston.2C_381.E2.80.93382:_Doris_Troy.2C_41:_David_Bromberg.2C_171:_Ronnie_Wood.2C_395:_Gary_Wright.2C_257.E2.80.93258:_Jeff_Lynne.2C_295.E2.80.93296:_Tom_Petty_257-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2003162.E2.80.93163:_Dylan.2C_121.E2.80.93125:_Eric_Clapton.2C_303.E2.80.93304:_Billy_Preston.2C_381.E2.80.93382:_Doris_Troy.2C_41:_David_Bromberg.2C_171:_Ronnie_Wood.2C_395:_Gary_Wright.2C_257.E2.80.93258:_Jeff_Lynne.2C_295.E2.80.93296:_Tom_Petty-257"><span>[</span>240<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Harrison
co-wrote
the
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Badge_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Badge
(song)">Badge</a>&quot;
with
Clapton,
which
was
included
on
<a
href="/wiki/Cream_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cream
(band)">Cream</a>'s
1969
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Goodbye_(Cream_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Goodbye
(Cream
album)">Goodbye</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng200653_258-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng200653-258"><span>[</span>241<span>]</span></a></sup>
Harrison
played
rhythm
guitar
on
the
track,
using
the
pseudonym
&quot;L'Angelo
Misterioso&quot;
for
contractual
reasons.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinn2009229_259-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinn2009229-259"><span>[</span>242<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
used
the
same
pseudonym
when
he
recorded
a
guitar
part
for
&quot;Never
Tell
Your
Mother
She's
Out
of
Tune&quot;,
a
song
from
<a
href="/wiki/Jack_Bruce?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jack
Bruce">Jack
Bruce</a>'s
1969
solo
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Songs_for_a_Tailor?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Songs
for
a
Tailor">Songs
for
a
Tailor</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinn2009289_260-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinn2009289-260"><span>[</span>243<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
May
1970
he
played
guitar
on
several
songs
during
a
recording
session
for
Dylan's
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/New_Morning?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
Morning">New
Morning</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2003283_261-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2003283-261"><span>[</span>244<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
addition
to
his
own
work,
between
1971
and
1973
he
co-wrote
and/or
produced
three
top
ten
hits
for
Starr:
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/It_Don%27t_Come_Easy?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="It
Don't
Come
Easy">It
Don't
Come
Easy</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Back_Off_Boogaloo?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Back
Off
Boogaloo">Back
Off
Boogaloo</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Photograph_(Ringo_Starr_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Photograph
(Ringo
Starr
song)">Photograph</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchaffner1980164_262-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchaffner1980164-262"><span>[</span>245<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1971
he
played
electric
slide
guitar
on
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/How_Do_You_Sleep%3F_(John_Lennon_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="How
Do
You
Sleep?
(John
Lennon
song)">How
Do
You
Sleep?</a>&quot;
and
a
<a
href="/wiki/Dobro?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dobro">dobro</a>
on
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Crippled_Inside?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Crippled
Inside">Crippled
Inside</a>&quot;,
both
from
Lennon's
<i><a
href="/wiki/Imagine_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Imagine
(album)">Imagine</a></i>
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng2006108.E2.80.93109_263-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng2006108.E2.80.93109-263"><span>[</span>246<span>]</span></a></sup>
Also
that
year,
he
produced
and
played
slide
guitar
on
Badfinger's
top
ten
hit
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Day_After_Day_(Badfinger_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Day
After
Day
(Badfinger
song)">Day
After
Day</a>&quot;,
and
a
dobro
on
Preston's
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Wrote_a_Simple_Song?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Wrote
a
Simple
Song">I
Wrote
a
Simple
Song</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-264"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-264"><span>[</span>247<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-266"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-266"><span>[</span>nb
18<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
worked
with
<a
href="/wiki/Harry_Nilsson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Harry
Nilsson">Harry
Nilsson</a>
on
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Son_of_Schmilsson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Son
of
Schmilsson">You're
Breakin'
My
Heart</a>&quot;
(1972)
and
with
<a
href="/wiki/Cheech_%26_Chong?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cheech
&amp;
Chong">Cheech
&amp;
Chong</a>
on
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Basketball_Jones_featuring_Tyrone_Shoelaces?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Basketball
Jones
featuring
Tyrone
Shoelaces">Basketball
Jones</a>&quot;
(1973).<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng2006140_267-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng2006140-267"><span>[</span>249<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1973
he
produced
and
made
a
guest
appearance
on
the
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Shankar_Family_%26_Friends?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Shankar
Family
&amp;
Friends">Shankar
Family
&amp;
Friends</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng2006138.2C_148.2C_169.2C_171.2C_328_268-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng2006138.2C_148.2C_169.2C_171.2C_328-268"><span>[</span>250<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
1974
Harrison
founded
<a
href="/wiki/Dark_Horse_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dark
Horse
Records">Dark
Horse
Records</a>.
In
addition
to
eventually
releasing
his
own
albums
on
the
label,
he
initially
used
the
company
as
an
avenue
for
collaboration
with
other
musicians.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2003147_269-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2003147-269"><span>[</span>251<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
wanted
Dark
Horse
to
serve
as
a
creative
outlet
for
artists,
as
Apple
Records
had
for
the
Beatles.<sup
id="cite_ref-270"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-270"><span>[</span>252<span>]</span></a></sup>
Harrison
explained:
&quot;Most
of
the
stuff
will
be
what
I
produce&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2003146_271-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2003146-271"><span>[</span>253<span>]</span></a></sup>
Eric
Idle
commented:
&quot;He's
extremely
generous,
and
he
backs
and
supports
all
sorts
of
people
that
you'll
never,
ever
hear
of.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoggett2009262_272-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoggett2009262-272"><span>[</span>254<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
first
acts
signed
to
the
new
label
were
Ravi
Shankar
and
<a
href="/wiki/Splinter?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Splinter">Splinter</a>,
whose
album
Harrison
produced,
which
provided
Dark
Horse
with
their
first
hit,
&quot;Costafine
Town&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-273"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-273"><span>[</span>255<span>]</span></a></sup>
Other
artists
signed
by
Dark
Horse
include
<a
href="/wiki/Attitudes_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Attitudes
(band)">Attitudes</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Henry_McCullough?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Henry
McCullough">Henry
McCullough</a>,
Jiva,
and
Stairsteps.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2003146.2C_149_274-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2003146.2C_149-274"><span>[</span>256<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Harrison
collaborated
with
Tom
Scott
on
Scott's
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/New_York_Connection?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
York
Connection">New
York
Connection</a></i>
(1976),
and
in
1981
he
played
guitar
on
&quot;Walk
a
Thin
Line&quot;,
from
<a
href="/wiki/Mick_Fleetwood?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mick
Fleetwood">Mick
Fleetwood</a>'s
<i>The
Visitor</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-275"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-275"><span>[</span>257<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1996
he
recorded
&quot;Distance
Makes
No
Difference
With
Love&quot;
with
Carl
Perkins,
and
played
slide
guitar
on
the
title
track
of
Dylan's
<i><a
href="/wiki/Under_the_Red_Sky?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Under
the
Red
Sky">Under
the
Red
Sky</a></i>
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2003109:_.22Distance_Makes_No_Difference_With_Love.22_384:_.27.27.5B.5BUnder_the_Red_Sky.5D.5D.27.27_276-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2003109:_.22Distance_Makes_No_Difference_With_Love.22_384:_.27.27.5B.5BUnder_the_Red_Sky.5D.5D.27.27-276"><span>[</span>258<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
2001
he
performed
as
a
guest
musician
on
Jeff
Lynne
and
Electric
Light
Orchestra's
comeback
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Zoom_(Electric_Light_Orchestra_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Zoom
(Electric
Light
Orchestra
album)">Zoom</a></i>,
and
on
the
song
&quot;Love
Letters&quot;
for
<a
href="/wiki/Bill_Wyman%27s_Rhythm_Kings?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bill
Wyman's
Rhythm
Kings">Bill
Wyman's
Rhythm
Kings</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuntley2006303.E2.80.93304_277-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuntley2006303.E2.80.93304-277"><span>[</span>259<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
also
co-wrote
a
new
song
with
his
son
Dhani,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Horse_to_the_Water?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Horse
to
the
Water">Horse
to
the
Water</a>&quot;,
which
was
recorded
on
1
October,
eight
weeks
before
his
death.
It
appeared
on
<a
href="/wiki/Jools_Holland?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jools
Holland">Jools
Holland</a>'s
album
<i>Small
World,
Big
Band</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2003119_278-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2003119-278"><span>[</span>260<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>During
the
Beatles'
American
tour
in
August
1965,
Harrison's
friend
<a
href="/wiki/David_Crosby?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="David
Crosby">David
Crosby</a>
of
the
Byrds
introduced
him
to
<a
href="/wiki/Indian_classical_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Indian
classical
music">Indian
classical
music</a>
and
the
work
of
<a
href="/wiki/Sitar?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sitar">sitar</a>
maestro
<a
href="/wiki/Ravi_Shankar?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ravi
Shankar">Ravi
Shankar</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng200620_279-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng200620-279"><span>[</span>261<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006147_280-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006147-280"><span>[</span>262<span>]</span></a></sup>
Harrison
described
Shankar
as
&quot;the
first
person
who
ever
impressed
me
in
my
life&nbsp;...
and
he
was
the
only
person
who
didn't
try
to
impress
me.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarrison2011216_281-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarrison2011216-281"><span>[</span>263<span>]</span></a></sup>
Harrison
became
fascinated
with
the
sitar
and
immersed
himself
in
<a
href="/wiki/Music_of_India?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Music
of
India">Indian
music</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006172_282-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006172-282"><span>[</span>264<span>]</span></a></sup>
According
to
Lavezzoli,
Harrison's
introduction
of
the
instrument
on
the
Beatles'
song
&quot;Norwegian
Wood&quot;
&quot;opened
the
floodgates
for
Indian
instrumentation
in
rock
music,
triggering
what
Shankar
would
call
'The
Great
Sitar
Explosion'
of
1966–67.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006171_283-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006171-283"><span>[</span>265<span>]</span></a></sup>
Lavezzoli
described
Harrison
as
&quot;the
man
most
responsible
for
this
phenomenon&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006171.E2.80.93172_284-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006171.E2.80.93172-284"><span>[</span>266<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-286"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-286"><span>[</span>nb
19<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
June
1966
Harrison
met
Shankar
at
the
home
of
Mrs
Angadi
of
the
Asian
Music
Circle,
asked
to
be
his
student,
and
was
accepted.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006176_287-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006176-287"><span>[</span>268<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
6
July,
Harrison
travelled
to
India
to
buy
a
sitar
from
Rikhi
Ram
&amp;
Sons
in
New
Delhi.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006176_287-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006176-287"><span>[</span>268<span>]</span></a></sup>
Lavezzoli
described
Harrison's
sitar
playing
on
the
<i>Revolver</i>
track
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Love_You_To?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Love
You
To">Love
You
To</a>&quot;
as
an
&quot;astonishing
improvement&quot;
over
&quot;Norwegian
Wood&quot;
and
&quot;the
most
accomplished
performance
on
sitar
by
any
rock
musician.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006175_288-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006175-288"><span>[</span>269<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
September,
he
returned
to
India
to
study
sitar
with
Shankar.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006176_287-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006176-287"><span>[</span>268<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
initially
stayed
in
Bombay,
then
moved
to
a
houseboat
on
a
remote
lake
where
Shankar
taught
him
for
six
weeks.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006176_287-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006176-287"><span>[</span>268<span>]</span></a></sup>
After
Shankar,
he
received
tutelage
from
Shambhu
Das.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett199971_289-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett199971-289"><span>[</span>270<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Harrison
studied
the
instrument
until
1968,
when
an
encounter
with
Clapton
and
Hendrix
at
a
hotel
in
New
York
convinced
him
to
put
down
the
instrument
and
return
to
guitar
playing.
He
commented:
&quot;I
decided&nbsp;...
I
should
get
back
to
the
guitar
because
I'm
not
getting
any
better
at
it,
and
I'm
not
going
to
be
a
great
sitar
player&nbsp;...
because
I
should
have
started
at
least
fifteen
years
earlier.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-290"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-290"><span>[</span>271<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

life</span>
<span

Personal

<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Hinduism">Hinduism</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a

Hinduism">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="thumb
tright">

Harrison,
Shyamasundara
Dasa
and











<a

in

of

Goswami">Jiva
Goswami</a>











<a

title="Samādhi"

in











<a
href="/wiki/Vrindavan?qsrc=3044"

title="Vrindavan">Vrindavan</a>,
India,
1996









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>By
the
mid-1960s
Harrison
had
become
an
admirer
of
<a
href="/wiki/Culture_of_India?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Culture
of
India">Indian
culture</a>
and
mysticism,
introducing
it
to
the
other
Beatles.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchaffner198077.E2.80.9378_291-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchaffner198077.E2.80.9378-291"><span>[</span>272<span>]</span></a></sup>
During
the
filming
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/Help!_(film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Help!
(film)">Help!</a></i>
in
the
Bahamas,
they
met
the
founder
of
<a
href="/wiki/Sivananda_Yoga?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sivananda
Yoga"
class="mw-redirect">Sivananda
Yoga</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Vishnudevananda_Saraswati?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Vishnudevananda
Saraswati">Swami
Vishnu-devananda</a>,
who
gave
each
of
them
a
signed
copy
of
his
book,
<i>The
Complete
Illustrated
Book
of
Yoga</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006173_292-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELavezzoli2006173-292"><span>[</span>273<span>]</span></a></sup>
Between
the
end
of
the
last
Beatles
tour
in
1966
and
the
beginning
of
the
<i>Sgt
Pepper</i>
recording
sessions,
he
made
a
pilgrimage
to
<a
href="/wiki/Mumbai?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mumbai">Bombay</a>
with
his
wife
Pattie,
where
he
studied
sitar,
met
several
<a
href="/wiki/Guru?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Guru">gurus</a>,
and
visited
various
holy
places.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoggett200933_293-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoggett200933-293"><span>[</span>274<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1968
he
travelled
to
<a
href="/wiki/Rishikesh?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rishikesh">Rishikesh</a>
in
northern
India
with
the
other
Beatles
to
study
meditation
with
<a
href="/wiki/Maharishi_Mahesh_Yogi?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Maharishi
Mahesh
Yogi">Maharishi
Mahesh
Yogi</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoggett200933_293-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoggett200933-293"><span>[</span>274<span>]</span></a></sup>
Harrison's
use
of
<a
href="/wiki/Psychedelic_drug?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Psychedelic
drug">psychedelic
drugs</a>
encouraged
his
path
to
meditation
and
Hinduism.
He
commented:
&quot;For
me,
it
was
like
a
flash.
The
first
time
I
had
<a
href="/wiki/Lysergic_acid_diethylamide?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lysergic
acid
diethylamide">acid</a>,
it
just
opened
up
something
in
my
head
that
was
inside
of
me,
and
I
realized
a
lot
of
things.
I
didn't
learn
them
because
I
already
knew
them,
but
that
happened
to
be
the
key
that
opened
the
door
to
reveal
them.
From
the
moment
I
had
that,
I
wanted
to
have
it
all
the
time—these
thoughts
about
the
yogis
and
the
Himalayas,
and
Ravi's
music.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGlazer197741_117-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGlazer197741-117"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Harrison
became
a
vegetarian
in
the
late
1960s,
and
a
devotee
of
the
Indian
mystic
<a
href="/wiki/Paramahansa_Yogananda?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Paramahansa
Yogananda">Paramahansa
Yogananda</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-294"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-294"><span>[</span>275<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
mid-1969,
he
produced
the
single
&quot;Hare
Krishna
Mantra&quot;,
performed
by
members
of
the
London
<a
href="/wiki/Radha?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Radha">Radha</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Krishna?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Krishna">Krishna</a>
Temple.
Soon
after,
Harrison
embraced
the
Hare
Krishna
tradition,
particularly
<i><a
href="/wiki/Japa?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Japa">japa-yoga</a></i>
chanting
with
beads,
and
became
a
lifelong
devotee.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPartridge2004153_295-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPartridge2004153-295"><span>[</span>276<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-297"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-297"><span>[</span>nb
20<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
respected
people
of
other
faiths
and
once
remarked:
&quot;All
religions
are
branches
of
one
big
tree.
It
doesn't
matter
what
you
call
Him
just
as
long
as
you
call.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETillery201178_298-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETillery201178-298"><span>[</span>278<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
commented
on
his
beliefs:</p>








<blockquote
class="templatequote">









<p>Krishna
actually
was
in
a
body
as
a
person&nbsp;...
What
makes
it
complicated
is,
if
he's
God,
what's
he
doing
fighting
on
a
battlefield?
It
took
me
ages
to
try
to
figure
that
out,
and
again
it
was
Yogananda's
spiritual
interpretation
of
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Bhagavad_Gita?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bhagavad
Gita">Bhagavad
Gita</a></i>
that
made
me
realise
what
it
was.
Our
idea
of
Krishna
and
<a
href="/wiki/Arjuna?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Arjuna">Arjuna</a>
on
the
battlefield
in
the
chariot.
So
this
is
the
point—that
we're
in
these
bodies,
which
is
like
a
kind
of
chariot,
and
we're
going
through
this
incarnation,
this
life,
which
is
kind
of
a
battlefield.
The
senses
of
the
body&nbsp;...
are
the
horses
pulling
the
chariot,
and
we
have
to
get
control
over
the
chariot
by
getting
control
over
the
reins.
And
Arjuna
in
the
end
says,
'Please
Krishna,
you
drive
the
chariot'
because
unless
we
bring
<a
href="/wiki/Jesus?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jesus">Christ</a>
or
Krishna
or
<a
href="/wiki/Gautama_Buddha?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gautama
Buddha">Buddha</a>
or
whichever
of
our
spiritual
guides&nbsp;...
we're
going
to
crash
our
chariot,
and
we're
going
to
turn
over,
and
we're
going
to
get
killed
in
the
battlefield.
That's
why
we
say
<span
style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span><i>Hare
Krishna,
Hare
Krishna</i><span
style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>,
asking
Krishna
to
come
and
take
over
the
chariot.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGlazer197739.E2.80.9340_299-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGlazer197739.E2.80.9340-299"><span>[</span>279<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








</blockquote>








<p>Before
his
religious
conversion,
the
only
British
performer
known
for
similar
activities
had
been
<a
href="/wiki/Cliff_Richard?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cliff
Richard">Cliff
Richard</a>,
whose
conversion
to
Christianity
in
1966
had
gone
largely
unnoticed
by
the
public.
&quot;By
contrast,&quot;
wrote
Inglis,
&quot;Harrison's
spiritual
journey
was
seen
as
a
serious
and
important
development
that
reflected
popular
music's
increasing
maturity&nbsp;...
what
he,
and
the
Beatles
had
managed
to
overturn
was
the
paternalistic
assumption
that
popular
musicians
had
no
role
other
than
to
stand
on
stage
and
sing
their
hit
songs.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInglis201011_300-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInglis201011-300"><span>[</span>280<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

Harrison's
house,











<a
href="/wiki/Kinfauns_(Surrey)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kinfauns
(Surrey)">Kinfauns</a>
in
Surrey,
which
he
shared
with
Pattie
Boyd









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>Harrison
married
the
model
<a
href="/wiki/Pattie_Boyd?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pattie
Boyd">Pattie
Boyd</a>
on
21
January
1966,
with
McCartney
as
<a
href="/wiki/Groomsman?qsrc=3044#Best_man"
title="Groomsman">best
man</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles2007210_301-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles2007210-301"><span>[</span>281<span>]</span></a></sup>
Harrison
and
Boyd
had
met
in
1964
during
the
production
of
the
film
<i>A
Hard
Day's
Night</i>,
in
which
the
19-year-old
Boyd
had
been
cast
as
a
schoolgirl.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoyd200760_302-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoyd200760-302"><span>[</span>282<span>]</span></a></sup>
They
separated
in
1974
and
their
divorce
was
finalized
in
1977.<sup
id="cite_ref-303"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-303"><span>[</span>283<span>]</span></a></sup>
Boyd
said
her
decision
to
end
their
marriage
and
leave
Harrison
was
due
largely
to
his
repeated
infidelities,
culminating
in
an
affair
with
Starr's
wife
<a
href="/wiki/Maureen_Starkey_Tigrett?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Maureen
Starkey
Tigrett">Maureen</a>,
which
Boyd
called
&quot;the
final
straw&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoyd2007179.E2.80.93180_304-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoyd2007179.E2.80.93180-304"><span>[</span>284<span>]</span></a></sup>
She
characterized
the
last
year
of
their
marriage
as
&quot;fuelled
by
alcohol
and
cocaine&quot;,
and
she
stated:
&quot;George
used
coke
excessively,
and
I
think
it
changed
him&nbsp;...
it
froze
his
emotions
and
hardened
his
heart.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoyd2007181_305-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoyd2007181-305"><span>[</span>285<span>]</span></a></sup>
She
subsequently
moved
in
with
Clapton,
and
they
married
in
1979.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoggett2009261_306-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoggett2009261-306"><span>[</span>286<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-308"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-308"><span>[</span>nb
21<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Harrison
married
Dark
Horse
Records'
secretary
<a
href="/wiki/Olivia_Harrison?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Olivia
Harrison">Olivia
Trinidad
Arias</a>
on
2
September
1978.
They
had
met
at
the
Dark
Horse
offices
in
Los
Angeles
in
1974,
and
together
had
one
son,
Dhani
Harrison,
born
on
1
August
1978.<sup
id="cite_ref-309"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-309"><span>[</span>288<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>He
restored
the
English
manor
house
and
grounds
of
Friar
Park,
his
home
in
<a
href="/wiki/Henley-on-Thames?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Henley-on-Thames">Henley-on-Thames</a>,
where
several
of
his
music
videos
were
filmed
including
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Crackerbox_Palace?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Crackerbox
Palace">Crackerbox
Palace</a>&quot;;
the
grounds
also
served
as
the
background
for
the
cover
of
<i>All
Things
Must
Pass</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGreene2006226.E2.80.93227_310-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGreene2006226.E2.80.93227-310"><span>[</span>289<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-313"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-313"><span>[</span>nb
22<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
employed
ten
workers
to
maintain
the
36-acre
(150,000&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>)
garden.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies2009360_314-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies2009360-314"><span>[</span>292<span>]</span></a></sup>
Harrison
commented
on
gardening
as
a
form
of
<a
href="/wiki/Escapism?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Escapism">escapism</a>:
&quot;Sometimes
I
feel
like
I'm
actually
on
the
wrong
planet,
and
it's
great
when
I'm
in
my
garden,
but
the
minute
I
go
out
the
gate
I
think:
'What
the
hell
am
I
doing
here?'&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarrison2011357_315-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarrison2011357-315"><span>[</span>293<span>]</span></a></sup>
His
autobiography,
<i><a
href="/wiki/I,_Me,_Mine_(book)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I,
Me,
Mine
(book)">I,
Me,
Mine</a></i>,
is
dedicated
&quot;to
gardeners
everywhere&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-316"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-316"><span>[</span>294<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
former
Beatles
publicist
<a
href="/wiki/Derek_Taylor?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Derek
Taylor">Derek
Taylor</a>
helped
Harrison
write
the
book,
which
said
little
about
the
Beatles,
focusing
instead
on
Harrison's
hobbies,
music
and
lyrics.<sup
id="cite_ref-317"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-317"><span>[</span>295<span>]</span></a></sup>
Taylor
commented:
&quot;George
is
not
disowning
the
Beatles&nbsp;...
but
it
was
a
long
time
ago
and
actually
a
short
part
of
his
life.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoggett2009266_318-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoggett2009266-318"><span>[</span>296<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Harrison
had
an
interest
in
<a
href="/wiki/Sports_car?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sports
car">sports
cars</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Motorsport?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Motorsport">motor
racing</a>;
he
was
one
of
the
100
people
who
purchased
the
<a
href="/wiki/McLaren_F1?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="McLaren
F1">McLaren
F1</a>
road
car.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBuckley2004127_319-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBuckley2004127-319"><span>[</span>297<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
had
collected
photos
of
racing
drivers
and
their
cars
since
he
was
young;
at
12
he
had
attended
his
first
race,
the
<a
href="/wiki/1955_British_Grand_Prix?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="1955
British
Grand
Prix">1955
British
Grand
Prix</a>
at
<a
href="/wiki/Aintree_Racecourse?qsrc=3044#Motor_racing"
title="Aintree
Racecourse">Aintree</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBuckley2004127_319-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBuckley2004127-319"><span>[</span>297<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-320"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-320"><span>[</span>298<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
wrote
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Faster_(George_Harrison_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Faster
(George
Harrison
song)">Faster</a>&quot;
as
a
tribute
to
the
<a
href="/wiki/Formula_One?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Formula
One">Formula
One</a>
racing
drivers
<a
href="/wiki/Jackie_Stewart?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jackie
Stewart">Jackie
Stewart</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Ronnie_Peterson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ronnie
Peterson">Ronnie
Peterson</a>.
Proceeds
from
its
release
went
to
the
<a
href="/wiki/Gunnar_Nilsson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gunnar
Nilsson">Gunnar
Nilsson</a>
cancer
charity,
set
up
after
the
Swedish
driver's
death
from
the
disease
in
1978.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuntley2006167_321-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuntley2006167-321"><span>[</span>299<span>]</span></a></sup>
Harrison's
first
extravagant
car,
a
1964
<a
href="/wiki/Aston_Martin_DB5?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Aston
Martin
DB5">Aston
Martin
DB5</a>,
was
sold
at
auction
on
7
December
2011
in
London.
An
anonymous
Beatles
collector
paid
&pound;350,000
for
the
vehicle
that
Harrison
had
bought
new
in
January
1965.<sup
id="cite_ref-322"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-322"><span>[</span>300<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Relationships_with_the_other_Beatles">Relationships
with
the
other
Beatles</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=George_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23"
title="Edit
section:
Relationships
with
the
other
Beatles">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>For
most
of
the
Beatles'
career
the
relationships
in
the
group
were
close.
According
to
<a
href="/wiki/Hunter_Davies?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hunter
Davies">Hunter
Davies</a>,
&quot;the
Beatles
spent
their
lives
not
living
a
communal
life,
but
communally
living
the
same
life.
They
were
each
other's
greatest
friends.&quot;
Harrison's
ex-wife
Pattie
Boyd
described
how
the
Beatles
&quot;all
belonged
to
each
other&quot;
and
admitted,
&quot;George
has
a
lot
with
the
others
that
I
can
never
know
about.
Nobody,
not
even
the
wives,
can
break
through
or
even
comprehend
it.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies2009325_323-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies2009325-323"><span>[</span>301<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Starr
said,
&quot;We
really
looked
out
for
each
other
and
we
had
so
many
laughs
together.
In
the
old
days
we'd
have
the
biggest
hotel
suites,
the
whole
floor
of
the
hotel,
and
the
four
of
us
would
end
up
in
the
bathroom,
just
to
be
with
each
other&quot;.
He
added,
&quot;there
were
some
really
loving,
caring
moments
between
four
people:
a
hotel
room
here
and
there
–
a
really
amazing
closeness.
Just
four
guys
who
loved
each
other.
It
was
pretty
sensational.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_Beatles2000357_324-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_Beatles2000357-324"><span>[</span>302<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Lennon
stated
that
his
relationship
with
Harrison
was
&quot;one
of
young
follower
and
older
guy&nbsp;...
[he]
was
like
a
disciple
of
mine
when
we
started.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESheff1981148_325-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheff1981148-325"><span>[</span>303<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
two
later
bonded
over
their
<a
href="/wiki/Lysergic_acid_diethylamide?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lysergic
acid
diethylamide">LSD</a>
experiences,
finding
common
ground
as
seekers
of
spirituality.
They
took
radically
different
paths
thereafter,
Harrison
finding
God
and
Lennon
coming
to
the
conclusion
that
people
are
the
creators
of
their
own
lives.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETillery2011122_326-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETillery2011122-326"><span>[</span>304<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1974
Harrison
said
of
his
former
bandmate:
&quot;John
Lennon
is
a
saint
and
he's
heavy-duty,
and
he's
great
and
I
love
him.
But
at
the
same
time,
he's
such
a
<i>bastard</i>
–
but
that's
the
great
thing
about
him,
you
see?&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarrison1975event_occurs_at_30_minutes_3.E2.80.9315_seconds_327-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarrison1975event_occurs_at_30_minutes_3.E2.80.9315_seconds-327"><span>[</span>305<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Harrison
and
McCartney
were
the
first
of
the
Beatles
to
meet,
having
shared
a
school
bus,
and
often
learned
and
rehearsed
new
guitar
chords
together.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInglis2010xiii.E2.80.93xiv_328-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInglis2010xiii.E2.80.93xiv-328"><span>[</span>306<span>]</span></a></sup>
McCartney
stated
that
he
and
Harrison
usually
shared
a
bedroom
while
touring.<sup
id="cite_ref-329"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-329"><span>[</span>307<span>]</span></a></sup>
McCartney
was
best
man
at
Harrison's
wedding
in
1966,
and
was
the
only
Beatle
in
attendance.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuntley200686_330-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuntley200686-330"><span>[</span>308<span>]</span></a></sup>
McCartney
has
referred
to
Harrison
as
his
&quot;baby
brother&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-331"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-331"><span>[</span>309<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
a
1974
BBC
radio
interview
with
<a
href="/wiki/Alan_Freeman?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alan
Freeman">Alan
Freeman</a>,
Harrison
stated:
&quot;[McCartney]
ruined
me
as
a
guitar
player&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBadman2001138.E2.80.93139_332-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBadman2001138.E2.80.93139-332"><span>[</span>310<span>]</span></a></sup>
Perhaps
the
most
significant
obstacle
to
a
Beatles
reunion
after
the
death
of
Lennon
was
Harrison
and
McCartney's
personal
relationship,
as
both
men
admitted
that
they
often
got
on
each
other's
nerves.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilmore200248_333-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilmore200248-333"><span>[</span>311<span>]</span></a></sup>
Rodriguez
commented:
&quot;even
to
the
end
of
George's
days,
theirs
was
a
volatile
relationship&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERodriguez201024_334-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERodriguez201024-334"><span>[</span>312<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Humanitarian_work">Humanitarian
work</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=George_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24"
title="Edit
section:
Humanitarian
work">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Harrison
was
involved
in
humanitarian
and
political
activism
throughout
his
life.
In
the
1960s,
the
Beatles
supported
the
<a
href="/wiki/Civil_rights_movement?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Civil
rights
movement"
class="mw-redirect">civil
rights
movement</a>
and
protested
against
the
<a
href="/wiki/Vietnam_War?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Vietnam
War">Vietnam
War</a>.
After
the
band's
break-up,
Ravi
Shankar
consulted
Harrison
about
how
to
provide
aid
to
the
people
of
Bangladesh
after
the
<a
href="/wiki/1970_Bhola_cyclone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="1970
Bhola
cyclone">1970
Bhola
cyclone</a>
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Liberation_War?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bangladesh
Liberation
War">Bangladesh
Liberation
War</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-theconcertforbangladesh1_335-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-theconcertforbangladesh1-335"><span>[</span>313<span>]</span></a></sup>
Harrison
recorded
the
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Bangla_Desh_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bangla
Desh
(song)">Bangla
Desh</a>&quot;,
and
pushed
Apple
Records
to
release
his
song
alongside
Shankar's
&quot;Joy
Bangla&quot;
in
an
effort
to
raise
funds.<sup
id="cite_ref-336"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-336"><span>[</span>314<span>]</span></a></sup>
Shankar
then
asked
for
Harrison's
advice
about
planning
a
small
charity
event
in
the
US.
Harrison
responded
by
organizing
the
Concert
for
Bangladesh,
which
raised
more
than
$240,000.<sup
id="cite_ref-337"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-337"><span>[</span>315<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
June
1972,
<a
href="/wiki/UNICEF?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a>
honoured
Harrison
and
Shankar
with
the
&quot;Child
Is
the
Father
of
Man&quot;
award
at
an
annual
ceremony
in
recognition
of
their
fundraising
efforts
for
Bangladesh.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBadman2001274_338-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBadman2001274-338"><span>[</span>316<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
George
Harrison
Humanitarian
Fund
for
UNICEF,
a
joint
effort
between
the
Harrison
family
and
the
US
Fund
for
UNICEF,
aims
to
support
programmes
that
help
children
caught
in
humanitarian
emergencies.<sup
id="cite_ref-unicefusa1_339-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-unicefusa1-339"><span>[</span>317<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
December
2007,
they
donated
$450,000
to
help
the
victims
of
Cyclone
Sidr
in
Bangladesh.<sup
id="cite_ref-unicefusa1_339-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-unicefusa1-339"><span>[</span>317<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
13
October
2009,
the
first
George
Harrison
Humanitarian
Award
went
to
Ravi
Shankar
for
his
efforts
in
saving
the
lives
of
children,
and
his
involvement
with
the
Concert
for
Bangladesh.<sup
id="cite_ref-340"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-340"><span>[</span>318<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="HandMade_Films">HandMade
Films</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=George_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25"
title="Edit
section:
HandMade
Films">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<div
class="rellink
relarticle
mainarticle">








Main
article:









<a
href="/wiki/HandMade_Films?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="HandMade
Films">HandMade
Films</a>







</div>








<p>In
1973
<a
href="/wiki/Peter_Sellers?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Peter
Sellers">Peter
Sellers</a>
introduced
Harrison
to
<a
href="/wiki/Denis_O%27Brien_(producer)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Denis
O'Brien
(producer)">Denis
O'Brien</a>.
Soon
after,
the
two
went
into
business
together.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2003211_341-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2003211-341"><span>[</span>319<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1978,
in
an
effort
to
produce
<i><a
href="/wiki/Monty_Python%27s_Life_of_Brian?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Monty
Python's
Life
of
Brian">Monty
Python's
Life
of
Brian</a></i>,
they
formed
the
film
production
and
distribution
company
HandMade
Films.<sup
id="cite_ref-342"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-342"><span>[</span>320<span>]</span></a></sup>
Harrison
explained:
&quot;The
name
of
the
company
came
about
as
a
bit
of
a
joke.
I'd
been
to
Wooky
Hole
in
Somerset&nbsp;...
[near]
an
old
paper
mill
where
they
show
you
how
to
make
old
underpants
into
paper.
So
I
bought
a
few
rolls,
and
they
had
this
watermark
'British
Handmade
Paper'&nbsp;...
So
we
said&nbsp;...
we'll
call
it
Handmade
Films.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2003211_341-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2003211-341"><span>[</span>319<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Their
opportunity
for
investment
came
after
<a
href="/wiki/EMI_Films?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="EMI
Films">EMI
Films</a>
withdrew
funding
at
the
demand
of
their
Chief
Executive,
<a
href="/wiki/Bernard_Delfont?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bernard
Delfont">Bernard
Delfont</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2003211.E2.80.93212_343-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2003211.E2.80.93212-343"><span>[</span>321<span>]</span></a></sup>
Harrison
financed
the
production
of
<i>Life
of
Brian</i>
in
part
by
mortgaging
his
home,
which
Idle
later
called
&quot;the
most
anybody's
ever
paid
for
a
cinema
ticket
in
history.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoggett2009262_272-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoggett2009262-272"><span>[</span>254<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
film
grossed
$21
million
at
the
box
office
in
the
US.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2003211_341-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2003211-341"><span>[</span>319<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
first
film
distributed
by
HandMade
Films
was
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Long_Good_Friday?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Long
Good
Friday">The
Long
Good
Friday</a></i>
(1980),
and
the
first
they
produced
was
<i><a
href="/wiki/Time_Bandits?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Time
Bandits">Time
Bandits</a></i>
(1981),
a
co-scripted
project
by
<a
href="/wiki/Monty_Python?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Monty
Python">Monty
Python</a><span
style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s
<a
href="/wiki/Terry_Gilliam?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Terry
Gilliam">Terry
Gilliam</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Michael_Palin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Michael
Palin">Michael
Palin</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2003212_344-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2003212-344"><span>[</span>322<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
film
featured
a
new
song
by
Harrison,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Dream_Away_(George_Harrison_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dream
Away
(George
Harrison
song)">Dream
Away</a>&quot;,
in
the
closing
credits.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInglis201083_345-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInglis201083-345"><span>[</span>323<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Time
Bandits</i>
became
one
of
HandMade's
most
successful
and
acclaimed
efforts;
with
a
budget
of
$5
million,
it
earned
$35
million
in
the
US
within
ten
weeks
of
its
release.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInglis201083_345-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInglis201083-345"><span>[</span>323<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Harrison
served
as
<a
href="/wiki/Film_producer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Film
producer">executive
producer</a>
for
23
films
with
HandMade,
including
<i><a
href="/wiki/Mona_Lisa_(film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mona
Lisa
(film)">Mona
Lisa</a></i>,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Shanghai_Surprise?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Shanghai
Surprise">Shanghai
Surprise</a></i>
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/Withnail_and_I?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Withnail
and
I">Withnail
and
I</a></i>.
He
made
several
<a
href="/wiki/Cameo_appearance?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cameo
appearance">cameo
appearances</a>
in
these
films,
including
a
role
as
a
nightclub
singer
in
<i>Shanghai
Surprise</i>,
for
which
he
recorded
five
new
songs.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng2006244_346-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng2006244-346"><span>[</span>324<span>]</span></a></sup>
According
to
author
and
musicologist
Ian
Inglis,
Harrison's
&quot;executive
role
in
HandMade
Films
helped
to
sustain
British
cinema
at
a
time
of
crisis,
producing
some
of
the
country's
most
memorable
movies
of
the
1980s.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInglis2010xvi_347-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInglis2010xvi-347"><span>[</span>325<span>]</span></a></sup>
A
series
of
<a
href="/wiki/Box_office_bomb?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Box
office
bomb">box
office
bombs</a>
in
the
late
1980s
caused
HandMade
to
cease
operations
in
1991;
three
years
later,
the
company
was
sold.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2003211.E2.80.93213_348-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2003211.E2.80.93213-348"><span>[</span>326<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Legacy">Legacy</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=George_Harrison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26"
title="Edit
section:
Legacy">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>In
1965
Harrison
and
the
other
Beatles
were
appointed
Members
of
the
Order
of
the
British
Empire
(<a
href="/wiki/Order_of_the_British_Empire?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Order
of
the
British
Empire">MBE</a>).
They
received
their
insignia
from
<a
href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Elizabeth
II">the
Queen</a>
at
an
investiture
at
Buckingham
Palace
on
26
October.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992203.E2.80.93204_349-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992203.E2.80.93204-349"><span>[</span>327<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1971
the
Beatles
received
an
<a
href="/wiki/Academy_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Academy
Award"
class="mw-redirect">Academy
Award</a>
for
the
best
Original
Song
Score
for
the
film
<i>Let
It
Be</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-academyaward_350-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-academyaward-350"><span>[</span>328<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
minor
planet
<a
href="/wiki/4149_Harrison?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="4149
Harrison">4149
Harrison</a>,
discovered
in
1984,
was
named
after
him.<sup
id="cite_ref-planet_351-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-planet-351"><span>[</span>329<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
December
1992
he
became
the
first
recipient
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_Music_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
Music
Award">Billboard
Century
Award</a>,
an
honour
presented
to
music
artists
for
significant
bodies
of
work.<sup
id="cite_ref-352"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-352"><span>[</span>330<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Rolling
Stone</i>
magazine
ranked
him
number
11
in
their
list
of
the
&quot;100
Greatest
Guitarists
of
All
Time&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPetty201158_210-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPetty201158-210"><span>[</span>194<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
2002,
on
the
first
anniversary
of
his
death,
the
<a
href="/wiki/Concert_for_George?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Concert
for
George">Concert
for
George</a>
was
held
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Royal
Albert
Hall">Royal
Albert
Hall</a>.
Clapton
organized
the
event,
which
included
performances
by
many
of
Harrison's
friends
and
musical
collaborators,
including
McCartney
and
Starr.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2003138.E2.80.93139_353-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2003138.E2.80.93139-353"><span>[</span>331<span>]</span></a></sup>
Eric
Idle,
who
described
Harrison
as
&quot;one
of
the
few
morally
good
people
that
rock
and
roll
has
produced&quot;,
performed
Monty
Python's
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_Lumberjack_Song?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Lumberjack
Song">Lumberjack
Song</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-354"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-354"><span>[</span>332<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
profits
from
the
concert
went
to
Harrison's
charity,
the
Material
World
Charitable
Foundation.<sup
id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2003138.E2.80.93139_353-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2003138.E2.80.93139-353"><span>[</span>331<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
2004
Harrison
was
posthumously
inducted
into
the
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame">Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame</a>
as
a
solo
artist
by
his
former
bandmates
Lynne
and
Petty,
and
into
the
Madison
Square
Garden
Walk
of
Fame
in
2006
for
the
Concert
for
Bangladesh.<sup
id="cite_ref-355"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-355"><span>[</span>333<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
14
April
2009,
the
Hollywood
Chamber
of
Commerce
awarded
Harrison
a
star
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hollywood
Walk
of
Fame">Walk
of
Fame</a>
in
front
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Capitol_Records_Building?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Capitol
Records
Building">Capitol
Records
Building</a>.
McCartney,
Lynne
and
Petty
were
present
when
the
star
was
unveiled.
Harrison's
widow
Olivia,
the
actor
<a
href="/wiki/Tom_Hanks?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tom
Hanks">Tom
Hanks</a>
and
Idle
made
speeches
at
the
ceremony,
and
Harrison's
son
Dhani
spoke
the
Hare
Krishna
mantra.<sup
id="cite_ref-356"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-356"><span>[</span>334<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
documentary
film,
<i><a
href="/wiki/George_Harrison:_Living_in_the_Material_World?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="George
Harrison:
Living
in
the
Material
World">George
Harrison:
Living
in
the
Material
World</a></i>,
was
directed
by
<a
href="/wiki/Martin_Scorsese?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Martin
Scorsese">Martin
Scorsese</a>
and
released
in
October
2011.
The
film
features
interviews
with
Olivia
and
Dhani
Harrison,
Klaus
Voormann,
<a
href="/wiki/Terry_Gilliam?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Terry
Gilliam">Terry
Gilliam</a>,
Starr,
Clapton,
McCartney,
<a
href="/wiki/Jim_Keltner?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jim
Keltner">Jim
Keltner</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Astrid_Kirchherr?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Astrid
Kirchherr">Astrid
Kirchherr</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-357"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-357"><span>[</span>335<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

&quot;<a

to
<i>Rubber

<li

gurus
<a

_matchUrl
=
"/afc-match?q=George_Harrison&page=1&ac=24&qid=F3E500D7E82094C982672AB154B676B1&qsrc=121&dm=&qrt=2&lid="+
"&o=0&l=dir&oo=&cl=ca-aj-cat&ch=cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN";





















_matchUrl+=
"&userip=76.78.3.114";




































_matchUrl+="&losid=a&locid=encw&lodid=us&loaid=a16";









var
location
=
window.location
+
"";








location
=
location.substring(7);








var
cutIdx
=
location.indexOf("/");








if
(location.indexOf(":")
>
-1)
{




















cutIdx
=
1
+
cutIdx
+
location.substring(cutIdx+1).indexOf("/");








}









var
urlPrefix
=
location.substring(0,
cutIdx);








_matchUrl
=
"http://"
+
urlPrefix
+
_matchUrl
+
"&afcec="
+
count
+
"&afcecb="
+
countBottom;








ajax_get(_matchUrl,
null,
null);




}





function
getXHR()
{








if
(window.XMLHttpRequest)
{












return
new
XMLHttpRequest();








}
else
if
(window.ActiveXObject)
{












try
{
















return
new
ActiveXObject("Msxml2.XMLHTTP");












}
catch
(e)
{
















try
{




















return
new
ActiveXObject("Microsoft.XMLHTTP");
















}
catch
(E)
{




















return
null;
















}












}








}








else
{












return
null;








}




}





function
ajax_get(url,
onsuccess,
onerror)
{








var
obj
=
getXHR();








if(obj)
{












obj.onreadystatechange
=
function()
{
















if(obj.readyState==4)
{




















if
(obj.status
==
200
&&
typeof(onsuccess)
==
"function")
{
























onsuccess(obj);




















}
else
if
(typeof(onerror)
==
"function")
{
























onerror(obj);




















}






















try
{
























delete
obj['onreadystatechange'];




















}
catch(e)
{}
















}












};












obj.open("GET",
url,
true,
"",
"");












obj.send(null);












return
obj;








}
else
{












if(onerror)
{
















onerror("Error
creating
XHR");












}
else
{
















a10.debug("Error
creating
XHR");












}












return
null;








}




}





afc_match();

</script>




</div>
